Fantasy • Ancient Style

Sunset Smoke

By Sienna Sunflower

Prologue

The sound of hooves echoed through the air as horsemen galloped across the lands. Grass flew in their wake as they gave chase to the brilliant streak of light tumbling through the sky. They chased it across vast green fields and over fog-shrouded mountains. Even the sea merchants floating on the water pointed at the light, shaking and turning to each other to confirm they were all seeing the same thing.

From the imperial palace to distant farms, people stopped to look up and stare. For a moment, the entire world watched the flash of light whirl across the heavens-a shooting star in daylight-arching toward the earth below.

And then, just like that, the light was gone. Time lurched back into motion, and people returned to their daily activities, whispering among themselves as they speculated about what sort of sign the star was. But not everyone had witnessed the light, for at that same moment, in a village hidden deep within the bamboo forests, a baby girl was born.

Chapter One

I opened my eyes to find myself in a maze of greenery, with bamboo stalks shooting up as far as the eye could see. I blinked a couple of times, marveling at how the sunlight filtering through the leaves cut through the fog.

Sunlight! I could feel my excitement grow as I looked around, eager to hurry over and take a closer look. Except . . . I couldn't move.

I had no physical form here. Not now, not yet.

I stared up at the leaves and let out a disappointed sigh. So much for exploring.

Suddenly, there was a rustle among the bamboo. My bubbly excitement returned as I waited for it to near. Would this be where I would meet my first friend?

Something brown and furry jumped out of the bushes. I looked at the animal, and the animal looked back, sniffing at me with its pink nose. A bunny! I laughed in delight. I had read about bunnies before, and now I could finally see one in person.

In a blink of an eye, I became the bunny. At first, the bunny seemed confused that a second soul was now inhabiting its body, but before long we found ourselves getting along quite well. I would go wherever the bunny went and could see through its eyes as it carried me through the forest.

It must have been a few days before the bunny finally ambled over to a clear stream to drink. There I noticed that the bunny's reflection wasn't entirely what I thought it would be. Poking out of the bunny's head, right in front of its fuzzy ears, were two little horns. My horns.

I inhaled sharply, and they vanished.

I spent the next few years letting the bunny carry me around the forest. Every morning, I breathed in the damp, misty air and relished the feeling of the mud on the forest floor beneath me.

Eventually, the bunny I was inhabiting began to slow down. Its movements weren't nearly as fast and light as before. And then one day, the bunny's soul vanished entirely, and I was left alone in its body. There were no longer two of us. It was just me as the bunny now.

I mourned the bunny's soul for three days and three nights before carrying on through the forest. I wandered aimlessly for many days before I came across the sound of footsteps.

I hid behind the stalks of bamboo, watching eagerly as the humans emerged from the trees. There were five of them, and all of them were male. Each of them had a quiver of arrows slung over their shoulders and held a bow in hand.

I watched as they passed by my hiding place and continued deeper into the forest. Once they vanished, I hopped over to the deep imprints their shoes had left in the dirt. There had to be more people where they came from, so I decided to follow the footsteps.

It didn't take me long to find the village, and it was difficult to contain my excitement as I hopped around, taking in all the wooden buildings. Despite the overall shabbiness of the village, if I listened carefully, I could hear the sounds of children laughing in the distance.

As I made to hop forward, my paws were suddenly flailing against open air as I was lifted upward. I squirmed and twisted around to find myself in the hands of a young girl.

"What do you think you're doing here?" the girl scolded as wriggled in her grasp. "If the villagers see you, you're going to end up as dinner!"

I stopped struggling and looked up at the girl. She couldn't have been more than seven years old.

The girl looked down at me as she cradled me in her arms. "Good bunny." She stroked my ears as she turned on her heel and walked me back into the surrounding forest. "Did you come all the way to the village because you were hungry? I'm sorry, I don't have any food on me right now. I'm going to take you back to the safety of the forest."

Once we were a good distance from the village, the girl gently set me down. Looking up at her now, I could see that her clothing was ragged and fraying. Dirt covered her face and was matted into her black hair. From the ground, I noticed the bruises peeking out from beneath the coarse fabric of her pants.

"There, there." The girl knelt down to pat me on the head. Even though her fingers were rough and callused, her touch was gentle. "You don't have to be afraid. You're safe now."

I looked up at the girl with wide eyes.

"I wish one day someone would save me," the girl said quietly. "Maybe if I was a bunny like you, everyone wouldn't bully me the way that they do."

I hesitantly hopped closer to the girl. The girl just sighed and took a seat on the forest floor. She tipped her head back, looking up at the sky high above. A soft wind picked up, sending fallen leaves swirling over the forest floor.

"I can't stay here long." The girl finally turned back to me. "Even though the other children push me around, I need to keep doing my best. I need to learn how to work. Then I can leave this village for good one day and finally begin my life."

I determinedly nodded my head to the girl's words.

The girl just blinked at me as she quickly leaned closer. "You-you can understand me?"

I nodded again.

The girl broke out into a smile as she jumped to her feet. She was practically dancing with excitement as she laughed. "I always knew I was the fated one! Look, look-even animals can understand me!"

Even though I had no clue what the girl was referring to, I hopped along with her. Her excitement was contagious.

Suddenly, there was the sound of quick footsteps coming from the path leading to the village. The girl must have noticed them too, because she immediately stopped dancing. Her smile faltered, and her entire posture caved. She quickly picked me up around the middle and set me behind a patch of bamboo before whirling around to face the path.

"Xia Yuxin!" A woman emerged. The lines of her face were harsh and stony, and she was dressed in the same patched and fraying clothing as the girl.

The girl, Yuxin, dropped her gaze to her feet.

"What do you think you're doing here?" the woman demanded as she seized Yuxin's arm and dragged her back toward the village. "Slacking off, are you now? I heard someone laughing in the forest. I thought I had gone crazy, but it turns out it was just you, you good-for-nothing daughter! If I could have it my way, I would have sold you early to anyone who offered a price!"

"Stepmother"-Yuxin let out a sob-"I was wrong. But the other children-"

"Talking back?" Yuxin's stepmother snapped as she harshly pinched her daughter's arm. Yuxin let out a pained cry before falling silent. Stealing a glance over her shoulder, Yuxin's tearful eyes met mine. Go home, she mouthed.

There wasn't anything I could do but watch sadly as the girl was dragged away.

I stayed hidden in the forest until the sun began to drop from the sky. Only when night fully engulfed the land did I silently creep back toward the path and into the village. Careful to stay out of sight, I hopped along the outskirts of the village, following the two sets of footprints that belonged to Yuxin and her stepmother. The footprints stopped at the entrance to a battered house. I moved around to the window at the back and leaped up onto the ledge. What I saw nearly made me fall backward in surprise.

Yuxin was lying face down on the floor, her dark hair spilling out in tangles around her. She seemed to be the only one in the small house, so I quickly hopped inside. I nuzzled Yuxin's hand with my nose, but she didn't move. I tried again, and this time the girl stirred.

Yuxin slowly sat up. She clasped her head, then hissed and dropped her hand to rub her behind. She blinked as her eyes fell on me. "Bunny!" After glancing around fearfully, she lowered her voice as she leaned over to whisper, "What are you doing here? You shouldn't be here!"

I just worriedly looked up at Yuxin. One of her eyes was swelling, and the color was already a shade of bluish-purple.

Yuxin offered me a pained smile. "I'm fine, really. You shouldn't worry about me-you should be worrying about yourself." After climbing to her feet, Yuxin leaned over to lift me up. She gently stroked my ears before setting me down on the windowsill. "Go on," she whispered. "Run away to freedom." There was something sad in her voice as she looked out at the forest beyond.

I looked at Yuxin, then to the forest, then back again.

She let out a sigh. "I can't go with you. One day I'll leave this place. But that day isn't today. There are still so many things I need to learn how to do; I can only write about twenty characters in total, and three of those belong to my name."

I still wouldn't leave, so Yuxin leaned over the windowsill and reached down to dip a bruised finger into one of the bowls collecting rainwater beneath it. "Yu," the girl said as she used the water to write on the wooden windowsill. "My late mother gave me the name 'jade' because she hoped that I would be able to bring wealth to the family when I grew up." She dipped her finger in the water and wrote again. "Xin. My mother chose the word 'heart' in the hope that I'd live a sincere life and be true to myself." By the time she had completed the last dot, the first character of "jade" was already beginning to fade.

I watched the lines the girl had drawn on the windowsill until they vanished completely.

"What about you?" Yuxin asked. "What's your name?"

I blinked up at her and tilted my head to the side.

Yuxin rested her arms on the windowsill. "Do you have a name?"

I shook my head.

"I'm not very good with coming up with names," Yuxin admitted. "I think Bunny works fine."

✦ ✦ ✦

When morning came, Yuxin stuck her head out the window and looked up at the golden sky. "Oh no! How long was I out?" I anxiously hopped from foot to foot as Yuxin quickly brushed loose strands of hair away from her face. She hurried toward the door, then paused as she looked over her shoulder. "Don't worry about me-go home to your family." After flashing me a final pained smile, Yuxin turned and hurried out of the tiny house.

Instead of leaving as Yuxin had instructed, I jumped down from the windowsill. I quickly caught up with her outside and watched as she slowed down in front of one of the houses. Just as I was about to hop over to her, the sound of running footsteps stopped me in my tracks.

"Xia Yuxin!" a mocking voice called.

Yuxin froze and slowly turned around to face the group of children who had come to a stop in front of her.

"Wow!" One of the children pointed a finger at Yuxin's swelling eye. "Who beat you up this time? Was it your stepmother or your father?"

Yuxin just remained silent as her posture caved.

"How many times do we have to tell you that we don't want to see your face around here?" The boy at the front of the group looked Yuxin up and down. "You're a curse who killed your own mother! We all hear the way your stepmother screams at you. If only you had been a boy and had been born a week later, you would have brought luck to us all instead of being such an inauspicious curse!"

Even though there was fear in Yuxin's eyes, she lifted her head. Throwing back her shoulders, she turned and silently walked away.

"Hey! Where do you think you're going?" a girl yelled angrily.

"Yeah!" one of the boys jumped in. "We're not done with you yet!"

Leaning down, the children picked up handfuls of stones from the ground and began hurling them at Yuxin.

Yuxin let out a cry and she threw her arms in front of her face as she was pelted with stones. I looked on in horror as Yuxin collapsed to the ground. She rolled into a ball as the stones continued to bounce off her.

At the sound of her cry, an older woman emerged from the house Yuxin had been standing in front of. "What do you children think you're doing?"

The children stopped throwing their stones immediately. Still shaking on the ground, Yuxin slowly poked her head out to look at her savior. But the moment the woman realized who was on the ground, her mouth became a hard line, and she turned and marched back into the house.

As soon as the woman vanished, the children once again began throwing their stones. When they finally grew bored, they turned and skipped off.

Even long after the children were gone, Yuxin continued to lie there in the dirt. I timidly hopped over to her and nuzzled against her hand. Instead of saying anything, she just wrapped me in her arms and held me tight.

✦ ✦ ✦

"I guess nothing I say will be able to convince you to go home," Yuxin said with a sigh as I sat next to her on the floor of her family's house. "If you want to stay, you can stay. Don't say I didn't warn you, though. If you really do get caught, I don't think I'll be able to save you."

I nodded. I knew how to be careful. I had made up my mind to stay. Even though a few hours had passed, I couldn't stop thinking about the way the village children had thrown stones at Yuxin.

"It's true that I was born on an inauspicious day," Yuxin said sadly as she stroked my fur. "It's also true that our village has gone through some hard times. When I was born, our village was flooded. That year, our village flooded not once but seven times. The fortune tellers say a demon arrived in our world that day. Now whenever something goes wrong, my stepmother will blame it on me. If it rains while the laundry is hanging outside, it's my fault. If she runs out of thread before she can finish patching her clothing, it's my fault. For a while, I lost all hope. Maybe all I'd ever be is a cursed child. But then the old man arrived at the village. He only stayed for a day, but he changed my life. He told all the village children that soon an evil will sweep over the lands. In turn, a female hero will rise up to subdue the evil, and then, once the demon has left the world for good, peace will return to all of us."

Demon? I hadn't come here to throw the human realm into turmoil. I didn't think I could even do so if I wanted; I had always been grouped among the lowest level demons. The extent of my magic was transformation, and even then I could only perform it on myself. And now, here in the human realm, I could already feel that magic fading.

"But that wasn't the part of the story that caught my attention," Yuxin continued. "The female hero who rises up to face down the demon-she's said to originally have been a girl with a cursed fate. Ever since that day, I've found myself thinking, Could that girl be me? Even if she isn't, she still gives me hope. If a girl like her can rise up and become a hero, I should at least be able to escape this village and start a new life for myself, right? I've found you, after all. Or maybe it was you who found me."

I just nuzzled up against Yuxin's hand, and she giggled as she scooped me up in her arms and hugged me tightly.

Suddenly, there was the sound of footsteps stomping into the house, and Yuxin quickly tucked me under a fraying basket. "Where were you off to this time?" It was Yuxin's stepmother.

This time a male voice answered. "I was just hunting with the other village men!"

"Liar!" Yuxin's stepmother shrieked. "You think your own wife wouldn't notice that you were gone for an entire week? What is it? Are you looking for another woman now because I can't live up to your late-"

There was the harsh sound of something making contact with flesh, followed by staggering footsteps.

"How dare you hit me!" the stepmother yelled.

"I've told you you're forbidden to talk about her like that!" Yuxin's father shouted over her curses. "Our late parents were the one who forced us together after my first wife passed away. You had one job, and that was to bare us a son! You call my daughter cursed, but I think you're the cursed one! Why have all our children died at birth? My late wife had one wish, and that was to raise her child in this village! But both of you make me sick. One of you killed my wife and the other has replaced her! So what if I want to escape this village for a short time and forget about all our troubles?"

There was a clap of thunder from outside, and they both fell silent as the skies opened up in a downpour.

"If you want to leave, then leave!" Yuxin's stepmother said heavily. I peered through the woven strips of the basket to see her clasping her cheek with one hand and pointing wildly at her husband with the other. "And take that curse of a daughter with you!"

"I don't want her!" Yuxin's father snapped. "You've been her mother since you married me! You're supposed to be responsible for her!"

As they argued back and forth, I finally mustered the courage to steal a glance at Yuxin, only to find that the girl had fallen asleep.

The initial happiness I had felt when I first arrived in the human realm had faded. I stood there, under the basket, shaking from the roar of the storm outside the house and the rage within it.

When morning finally came, the rain stopped just as quickly as it had started. After breakfast, Yuxin hid me in the basket of laundry she was taking down to the stream. At the stream, she got to work washing and beating the garments in the wooden bucket that was already waiting there on the rocks.

"This is how you wash the clothing," Yuxin explained to me in an undertone. "You just beat it and beat it and beat it . . ." I watched as Yuxin continued to hit the clothes with a stick. She finally stopped, completely spent as she flopped over backward to stare up at the sky. Yuxin reached up with a hand as if she could grasp the sky and the bamboo leaves swaying back and forth before the infinite blue sea. "This is the only work they allow me to do here. They won't let me do any cooking-they won't let me get close to any sort of fire. Everyone here knows I'm the unlucky child, and they don't want to take any chances with me burning the village down."

I hopped up onto Yuxin's stomach, and she giggled as wrapped her arms around me.

She let out a sigh as she absently ran a hand through my fur. "You don't know how lucky I feel that we have each other now. One day we'll leave this place together, Bunny. Our lives have yet to begin."

✦ ✦ ✦

Over the next few years, I followed Yuxin everywhere she went. At night, when the entire village was asleep, I would silently hop into the forest and work on making a human form for myself. My inner force had never been very strong to begin with, but I wouldn't give up.

As a bunny, I could only do so much for Yuxin. I couldn't talk or voice any of my thoughts or commiserations. I wanted a pair of arms for myself so I could hold her the way she would hold me through the stormy nights. I wanted to be human. I wanted to be a girl like Yuxin.

Every night I would cultivate my power. And every night I would fail to transform myself into a human. But I wouldn't stop trying. I was determined to help Yuxin. At the end of the third year, I finally succeeded.

This time, when the light faded, I was lying on the forest floor. My mind felt fuzzy, and I blinked up in a daze at the stars glittering in the night sky above. My fingers twitched as they brushed against something soft. Fingers! I-I have fingers!

I sat bolt upright, holding my new hands out in front of me in excitement. I reached up and touched my face. I ran a hand through my long black hair.

Feeling the soft sensation in my fingers, I turned and looked down at the lifeless body of the bunny I once inhabited. I smiled sadly; it was like saying goodbye to an old friend. I no longer needed a host; I had created a body for myself.

I buried the bunny's corpse before shakily climbing to my feet. Finally, I used the last of my meager power to clothe myself in a dress like the ones worn by the people in the village. I could feel my magic flickering out, and this time, when I tried to call on it, it wouldn't respond. But I didn't mind, because from this day forward, I would be a human.

I took a step toward the village but staggered as the world swayed. My eyelids were drooping, and I blinked rapidly to stay awake. With my power used up, I felt lethargic, and my mind was filling with fog. I had never slept before, but as I curled up on the forest floor, with the entire world bathed in silvery moonlight, sleep had never sounded better.

Chapter Two

"You! Yes, you! Don't think we don't see you hiding!" The voices echoed as I drifted among the rafters of the library, but they were only calling out because they, as a matter of face, couldn't find me. I had just started reading a new story, and I wanted to get to the end before it was time to get back to work.

"Found you!" a voice called triumphantly.

I nearly toppled off the rafters in surprise. As I floated there in the air, the other demons drifted up to meet me. Their dark, smoke-like bodies blended together as they formed a circle around me.

"Reading about the human realm again?" one of the demons asked as it snatched the book from me.

"Hey!" I flew forward to grab the book back, but the demons encircling me swooped forward like a solid wall, and I was tossed backward.

"This is about the human realm?" Another demon laughed as they tossed the book back and forth between themselves. "What's so good about the human realm?"

"The human realm has heroes," I said confidently as I continued to struggle for the book.

"Heroes?" The demons looked at each other before bursting out into guffaws. "Don't tell us that you want to be a hero," one of the demons snickered. "You could never be a hero. In fact, you couldn't even be the villain. Maybe if you're lucky, you'll get to be the villain's sidekick!"

At this point, I had given up trying to get my book back. "Do all of you have nothing better to do? I thought you didn't like the library. If Lady Hui finds you here, you're all going to get in trouble."

As if on cue, a figure in flowing white robes glided into the long halls of the library. The demons around me shrieked as they quickly scattered. I caught my book as the demons tossed it into the air in their haste.

"You," Lady Hui said coldly. "Come down here."

I dejectedly floated down to the woman in the white.

Lady Hui reached out with a pale, long-fingered hand to snatch the book from me. "You good-for-nothing demon," she scoffed as she flipped through the pages of the book.

"Lady Hui, please," I pleaded as she grabbed me by one of the horns sticking out of my head and began dragging me toward the door, "I'm not causing any trouble. You know I've always done my job. Look, none of the ghosts I'm responsible for have ever escaped! I've already finished my work for the day. Please, let me stay here-"

Lady Hui just ignored my words and tossed me out of the library. She didn't even bother closing the doors as she turned on her heel and glided back inside the gigantic building.

I just floated there outside the library for a long time. I stared longingly at the books inside, but I wasn't one to break the rules twice in one day. I was just glad Lady Hui didn't tell the demon lord about my habits. Lady Hui was the demon lord's favorite. She was a painted-skin ghost and had apparently snatched the skin of the most beautiful woman in the human realm for herself some hundred years ago. Lady Hui and the other painted-skin ghosts were exceptions here in the demon realm. The vast majority of the other ghosts were creatures of nightmares.

I drifted away from the library. My mind was still on the book I had been reading, and since I doubted I'd be able to get it back from Lady Hui any time soon, I decided to make up my own ending for it. The pair of sisters in the story would each marry their true loves and live happily forever.

✦ ✦ ✦

It seemed only a moment had passed since I closed my eyes, but the next moment, I found myself being shaken awake. The sunlight streaming through the bamboo hit me full in the face as I opened my eyes.

"Hey!" a familiar voice called worriedly. "Are you alright?"

My grogginess instantly vanished as my eyes fell on the bruised hand gently shaking my arm. I sat bolt upright and squinted against the light. "Yuxin!" I practically laughed out loud.

"You know me?" Yuxin's eyes were wide. "I don't think I've ever seen you before."

"I'm Bunny!" I beamed.

Yuxin's mouth fell open. "Bunny?"

I nodded energetically as Yuxin gave herself only a moment's hesitation before throwing her arms around me in a tight hug. "I can't believe it!" Yuxin was half laughing, half crying. "But how?" Yuxin shook her head as she drew back to look at me in awe. "You must be a bunny spirit from the heavens. Did you spend hundreds of years cultivating a human form? Either way, it doesn't matter how. I always believed miracles could happen. And look-you're a human now!"

"I wanted to be a human like you." I took Yuxin's hands in my own as I held her gaze. "I didn't want you to have to suffer alone."

"Bunny," Yuxin sniffled, her eyes full of emotion, "with you there with me, I was never alone."

When we both calmed down, I asked, "What are you doing out here in the forest?"

"I was looking for you, of course," Yuxin said matter-of-factly. "I was worried that something happened to you-worried my own bad luck put you in danger."

I held Yuxin's gaze. "Nothing bad has happened to me over these past few years with you. I don't think you're unlucky. The only unlucky part is how you were born into this village. Remember how you always told me that one day you'd leave this village behind? I'll go with you."

"Soon," Yuxin said quietly, determinedly. "Soon we'll begin our new life." She took me by the hand and helped me to my feet. She squinted at me for a moment before blinking in astonishment. "It's so amazing! You actually look a little bit like me. We could be sisters!"

"I wanted to be a girl like you," I explained. "And finally it worked!"

"I don't know what will happen if we bring you into the village." Yuxin's smile faded. "I don't know if any of the villagers would let you stay with them either."

"That's fine. I can just stay in the forest."

"But what about food and shelter? Besides, you know how unpredictable the rain here is."

"It's fine, I . . ." I trailed off as my stomach gave a loud rumble.

Yuxin tugged me toward the path to the village. "It's better risking what the villagers will say than starving to death."

I nodded as I followed Yuxin out of the forest. Even though I had spent the past few years sneaking among the villagers, this was the first time they would be meeting me in person. I knew all about them, but they never even suspected my existence.

As we entered the village, the ambling villagers looked up from whatever they were doing to glance at me. Despite feeling uneasy from their stares, I tried my best to offer them a smile. After Yuxin explained to the villagers that I had been separated from my traveling party and that she found me in the forest, the villagers grudgingly agreed to let me stay with the other village orphans.

After a few days passed, it became clear that the villagers weren't fond of my presence, especially since I always followed Yuxin around. And I was another mouth to feed. Even though they didn't say anything to my face, I could feel their eyes on me whenever I walked past, as if they were silently wishing for me to vanish.

"I've decided, Bunny," Yuxin told me in an undertone as we sat on the wooden steps of her house, "we're going to leave this week."

"This week?" I exclaimed.

"Shh!" Yuxin held a finger to her lips, glancing around to make sure no one was listening. "We'll need food for our journey, and we'll need money. I'll start setting aside a few things for us to take with us. As for money . . . I'm not going to steal it from the other villagers. I know how to wash clothing. We can work for it along the way."

I nodded confidently. "I'll help you."

Yuxin sighed as she rested her head on my shoulder. "With every passing day, my will to leave this place just grows stronger and stronger. I'm done living as the curse of the village. I'm done being my parents' unwanted child. I know that my stepmother wants to sell me the first chance she gets, and with my father coming home less and less often, I fear she will take her chances any day now."

"Let's leave tomorrow, then," I suggested. "We can leave in the middle of the night, and we'll be long gone before the villagers wake up."

I could hear the resolve in Yuxin's voice. "Let's do it."

✦ ✦ ✦

Under the cover of night, I carefully crawled out from between the two children I'd been sleeping next to at the orphan shelter. Then, after silently grabbing my shoes, I made my way down the path running through the middle of the village. Yuxin was already waiting for me at the entrance of the forest.

"Bunny!" Yuxin beckoned me over with an excited whisper. "Are you ready to go?"

I nodded my head. "I'm ready."

We walked for hours following the forest path. The moon was our only source of light, and the fog was so thick it was difficult to tell what was lying in the distance.

"Are you afraid?" Yuxin asked.

I shook my head. "I'm not afraid. I'm not afraid of anything. Well, except your parents."

"I've never gone this far into the forest before," Yuxin whispered. "I'm scared. But I'm also excited. I've been waiting for this day for years. Beyond this forest, there will be no more late night arguments from my parents. There will be no more stone-throwing children."

"We'll work for our own success!" I said as I skipped down the path. "We'll start small with our laundry business, and then once we've saved enough money, we can travel to a bigger city and continue the business there."

"Yes!" Yuxin laughed. "And then we'll be able to live comfortably and do whatever we want to do."

"But what happens if you are the female hero from the story that old man told you?" I turned around to face Yuxin, walking backward down the dirt path. "Would you still be willing to open a laundry business with me?"

Yuxin giggled at that. "Even if I am the hero, I'll still need money!"

I laughed too, and then Yuxin took me by the hand, and we sprinted down the path together.

When the sky slowly began to lighten, Yuxin and I finally came to a stop. We took a seat off to the side of the path, and Yuxin opened the sack she had brought with her. She pulled out a steamed bun and split it in half. She handed me a portion, and I took it happily. "Yum!"

Yuxin burst into laughter at that. "I wish I could live as simple a life as you, Bunny. Even these flavorless buns the village ladies make can make you happy."

"Why shouldn't they make me happy?"

Yuxin was silent as she looked sadly down at the bun she held in her hands.

I placed a reassuring hand on her shoulder. The coarse fabric of her top was rough under my fingers.

"Here." Yuxin took my hand and pressed the remaining portion of her bun into it.

"But what about you?" I tried my best to give it back.

Yuxin just shook her head as she hopped out of my reach. "I think it will bring you more happiness than it will bring me. I'm not hungry anyway."

"I'm not hungry either." I quickly shook my head as I tried again to hand it back. But my treacherous stomach let out a rumble.

"Just eat it!" Yuxin laughed. "You can't fool me that easily."

I sighed, but I was smiling all the same. "Okay, okay."

After our brief break, the two of us continued on our way. The forest was silent save for the sound of the wind whispering through the leaves.

"My parents probably noticed that we're gone by now," Yuxin commented absently.

I suddenly frowned. "You're right. If they follow our footprints, well, our footprints will lead them right to us."

"I don't think they care enough about us to give chase," Yuxin said thoughtfully. "I don't think they'll try and follow us."

Around our second day of walking, the bamboo began to thin out. After we left the forest completely, the two of us walked down the dirt path toward a small collection of buildings in the distance. The sun beat down on us from overhead, and the closer we got, the more people joined us on the path. Horse-drawn carts rolled past us, and Yuxin and I looked on in awe.

"We did it!" Yuxin grabbed my hands as she jumped up and down. She pulled me along, and the two of us ran the rest of the way down the path and into the town.

With wide eyes, I took in all the wood and brick of the buildings that lined the streets.

When we finally came to a stop in the center of the town, Yuxin seemed to have gotten over her initial rush of excitement. "If the villagers really do come looking for us, we can only stay here for a few days at most. I think this town is big enough that if someone does show up, it would probably take them some time to find us."

Yuxin and I spent the majority of the afternoon walking through the town, admiring the buildings and the bustle. Street vendors were calling out their products, and Yuxin and I stopped many a time to ogle at the little ornaments and trinkets being sold.

By the time the sun began to set, the two of us headed over to the river that ran through the middle of the town to rest for the night. We decided to take turns sleeping and keeping an eye out for anyone who might be looking for two runaway girls around the age of ten. Fortunately, no one showed up to bother us throughout the night.

We spent the following morning begging people for money on the streets. It took a few hours, but we finally gathered enough coins to buy us a cheap wooden bucket, a laundry paddle, some powdered soap, and a couple of steamed buns.

We returned to the river and sat down to eat. "How do you think we can attract customers?" I asked between bites.

"We could yell out at people the way the street vendors do." Yuxin frowned slightly as she bit into her bun. "We just need enough money to last us as we travel to the next town."

I turned the wooden bucket I had bought upside down before hopping up on top of it. "Washing clothes!" I called out as I cupped my hands to my mouth. "Washing clothes!"

Yuxin giggled as I jumped up and down on the bucket, waving my hands at anyone who walked past. "Be careful!"

For the first half of the day, it seemed like we really weren't going to get any customers. Yuxin and I sat back to back by the river. Our initial excitement of arriving at the town had begun to wear off, and we were beginning to feel the anxiousness set in.

Just as we felt like losing hope, a middle-aged man came to a stop in front of us. Yuxin and I both looked up at him, and my eyes went immediately to the sword strapped to his back. The man seemed to notice where I was looking and chuckled. "Are you girls doing laundry? It just so happens that my overcoat needs a good washing."

"Yes!" I quickly jumped to my feet and pulled Yuxin up along with me.

The man handed me his coat, and Yuxin quickly filled our wooden bucket with water from the river. As Yuxin began washing the garment, the man dropped a few coins into my hand before taking a seat on the stone path. "What are you girls doing out here all by yourselves? Where are your parents?"

"We're orphans," Yuxin said.

"Orphans," the man echoed.

"We just arrived in town," I explained as I took a seat next to Yuxin. "We have no money and no one to rely on except for each other."

"Are you two sisters?" the man asked. "The two of you look quite similar."

Yuxin nodded. "That's right. We're sisters."

I turned back to look at the man. "Do you live here?"

"Me?" The man laughed. "No, no. I'm just passing through."

"You're a martial artist!" I said excitedly. "You have to be!"

"I am," the man said matter-of-factly. "It's true that I'd consider myself part of the martial arts world, but even after all these years, I'm no master."

"What's it like?" I asked eagerly.

The man chuckled. "Well, if you want to hear a long story, you've come to the right person."

Yuxin and I listened in awe as the man told us the story of one of his many adventures. The two of us were completely mesmerized by his tale. Even after Yuxin finished washing his overcoat and set it aside to dry, the man continued to sit with us, quite content in reliving his adventures.

As he talked, other people wandered over to us, and we had a grand total of five customers that day. By the time the man finished his stories, the sun had begun to dip from the sky, and the clouds above were painted with pinks and oranges and reds.

"Still a little damp," the man remarked as he felt the fabric of his overcoat. "How about we get something to eat? I'll pay."

"We couldn't!" Yuxin and I protested, but the man brushed us off.

"You listened to me talk for so long-it would only make sense to pay you back for your time."

After Yuxin and I carefully stashed away our laundry supplies in an alleyway, the man took us to one of the restaurants, and despite our protests, bought each of us a bowl of noodles.

The man sighed as we took a seat at the back of the restaurant and set his sword down next to our table. "I happen to be an orphan myself. And we orphans got to look out for each other, no?"

"When did you decide to join the martial arts world?" I asked as we waited for our noodles to arrive.

"Oh, it was many, many, years ago. When you're an orphan, there are only so many paths you can take when it comes to survival. I chose my path, and I hope the two of you choose wisely when it comes to yours."

I fell silent after that as a waiter hurried over to our table with our food.

"Are there many female heroes in the martial arts world?" Yuxin asked as she eagerly reached for her chopsticks.

"Female heroes?" the man echoed. "There are quite many of them. Why, do you want to join the martial arts world?"

"Do you know if there are heroes in the martial arts world that are powerful enough to subdue a demon? Is it even possible to subdue a demon? Do demons even exist?"

"Demons?" The man blinked. His chopsticks were halfway to his mouth when he paused. "Are you talking about that story that's being spread around? It's just a bunch of nonsense if you ask me."

"Nonsense?" Yuxin finished slurping up another mouthful of noodles before turning to face the man. "You don't believe that a demon will appear?"

"I find it hard to believe." The man frowned faintly at the noodles that had slipped out of his grasp and fallen back into his bowl. "There's always rumors and stories like that being spread through the martial arts world. Only ten or twenty percent of the time do they ever hold any truth. I hope I can offer the two of you some advice before we part, though: Don't enter the martial arts world if you wish to live a long life. People like us are lucky if we can live beyond twenty-five years old."

"But you must be at least fifty!" I piped up.

The man let out an exasperated noise. "That's because I'm lucky. And do I really look that old? I'm thirty-one! Thirty-one, I tell you! I've had my fair share of near-death experiences, and I've lost many dear brothers along the way. The human heart and mind are never guaranteed to stay the same. That kind of life will change you."

After a long silence, I said, "We'll take your word for it."

When we were done with our meal, the man walked us back out onto the streets. "Where are you girls off to?" He had put his overcoat on and strapped his sword to his back.

"We want to go that way." I pointed in the direction of the path leading out of the town.

"We don't plan to stay here in this town for long," Yuxin added. "We wanted to try and make enough money to last us until we get to the next town."

The man sighed. "I would offer to escort the two of you, but I just came from that direction. I cleared out all the bandits on the way too, mind you. Traveling should be safe enough for the next couple of days. But I'm heading that way, you see." He pointed in the opposite direction. "There's a small village in the middle of the forest that I'm supposed to pass through on my way to my destination."

Yuxin and I exchanged a glance. That was where the two of us had just come from.

"You girls shouldn't stay out here on the streets." The man pulled out a sack of coins and poured a very generous amount onto his hand. He held the coins out to Yuxin and me. "Take the money, and use it to find someplace to stay tonight. The rest of it can be used to aid you on your journey."

Yuxin and I protested against accepting the money, but when the man persisted, both of us profusely thanked him again for everything.

The man gave us a smile and a wave. "Maybe we'll see each other again. Or maybe before we meet, my luck will have finally run out, and if you want to see me then, you'll have to visit my grave. The name's Wu Ren. Remember it." And then he was off, walking away from us as he made his way down the slowly emptying street.

We watched him until he completely vanished from view. Only then did Yuxin and I turn to each other. Yuxin's expression was that of shock, as if she still couldn't believe what had happened. "Hero Wu . . ."

"I know." I shook my head in disbelief.

"Come on." Yuxin took me by the arm as she finally recovered. "Let's go find a place to sleep."

Even though Yuxin struggled to make out the characters on the signs, I knew how to read, and I quickly directed the two of us to a hotel. On the ground story, customers still sat around at the tables drinking. Slipping past them, Yuxin mustered the courage to ask one of the workers if we could get a small room for the night. At first, the worker seemed skeptical of us two kids, but when Yuxin held out the money to him, he just waved us in the direction of the stairs.

Our room was tiny. The floor was covered in dirty shoe prints, and the smell of unwashed clothes lingered in the air. I wrinkled my nose as I walked over to open the window in the back of the room.

Instead of sleeping on the filthy bed, Yuxin and I curled up in the corner of the room. Laying side by side on the floor, the warmth of our bodies kept us warm through the night.

✦ ✦ ✦

In the morning, I glanced back over my shoulder at the buildings as the two of us walked down the road leading out of the town. "How many days do you think it will take to get to the next town?"

"It can't be more than a week's worth of walking," Yuxin said thoughtfully. "We should have enough food."

"We won't really run into bandits, will we?"

"Didn't Hero Wu say he cleared them out?" Yuxin said, but her tone was unconfident.

Keeping our eyes peeled as we walked, the two of us moved as swiftly as possible toward the next town. Along the way, we were able to pay a farmer to let us hitch a ride on his wooden cart. Traveling with the farmer felt much safer, and we both thanked him when we arrived in the town.

"Look!" I pointed excitedly at the buildings. Flowers bloomed in every direction, and bridges arched over the waterways.

Yuxin jumped up and down in excitement. "Bunny, if we could settle here, wouldn't that be perfect? Knowing my parents, even if they did look for us in that first town, they'd give up quickly when they realized that we're not there."

"Let's go set up our business!" I took Yuxin by the hand, and together we hurried down to the waterways snaking through the city.

For the next few days, Yuxin and I spent our time washing clothing. Our shared pouch of money was gradually becoming heavier and heavier. Every night, the two of us would retire to one of the cheaper hotels.

"Twenty-one, twenty-two, twenty-three . . ." I counted our coins from where I lay propped up on my elbows on the bed. Yuxin lay next to me as she watched me drop each coin back into the pouch.

Yuxin tugged on a strand of her long black hair. "When we get to one hundred, we should buy ourselves some new clothes."

I nodded my head as I dropped the last of our coins back into the pouch. "Agreed!"

"We still have that martial artist to thank for giving us the funds to actually keep our little business going." Yuxin sighed. "I feel bad that we can't repay him."

"Me too," I said sadly as I reached up to undo my hair.

"In no time, we'll have our own shop!" Yuxin said determinedly. "By that time, we'll be living a good life."

I smiled at that.

"I've always wanted a sister," Yuxin admitted as she sat up.

I sat up as well and wrapped my arms around Yuxin in a warm hug. "Well, you've got one now. We'll be sisters forever!"

"We'll be together forever!" Yuxin giggled. "We'll grow up together, and after we've found boys to love here in this city, we could have a double wedding!"

"I like the sound of that." I laughed as I let go of Yuxin. In the demon realm, love didn't exist. But now that I was here in the human realm, would I fall in love like all the heroes in the stories I read? When would I fall in love? How would I know when the time came?

Yuxin elbowed me. "What are you thinking about?"

I offered Yuxin my little finger. "Sisters forever?"

Yuxin's smile lit up her entire face as she met my finger with her own. "Sisters forever."

✦ ✦ ✦

The next month went smoothly enough. However, when it came to finding a place where we could open a shop for ourselves, after talking among ourselves, Yuxin and I decided it was much more realistic to find someone who would hire us.

We took a break from washing laundry by the waterways to search for anyone who might be hiring laundry girls. "Bunny," Yuxin said tiredly. "Do you think we're really going to make it here?" The two of us were leaning against the railing of an arched bridge.

"We're going to," I said confidently as we gazed out over the bustling waterways and streets. "We've only been here for a month-of course we're going to start off small." When Yuxin still looked discouraged, I took her hand and gave it a squeeze. "Come, today will be the day when we actually buy ourselves some new clothes."

Yuxin returned the smile as I led her over the bridge and down the street beyond. As the two of us made our way to the clothing shop, I suddenly realized that the streets were empty. Normally they were always bustling, and now they were silent. I slowed to a stop, tugging on Yuxin's sleeve.

"Where is everyone?" I whispered.

Yuxin paused for a moment, then picked up her pace. Her fingers tightened around mine. "Let's move quickly."

But before we could make it halfway down the street, a deep male voice called out from behind us. "Are you girls lost?"

Yuxin and I spun around. Three men were standing in the middle of the street, and the man at the front took a step forward. Even though he looked like an ordinary townsperson, there was just something about his energy that sent a shiver down my spine.

The man extended a hand to us. "Come here."

Yuxin took a step back. She tugged me along with her.

"Be good girls," the man said, but an impatience had filled his voice.

"Can't we just capture them now?" One of the men standing behind him asked. "We've been following them all week. We finally managed to clear the townspeople away from this street, but our men can't keep them away for long."

"Capture us?" I asked faintly.

"What do you want?" Yuxin demanded, trembling.

"Get them!" commanded the man at the front, and the other two men sprinted forward.

Yuxin and I screamed. We whirled around only to find three more men running at us from the opposite side of the street. Yuxin's eyes met mine. If we wanted to escape, we needed to split up and make a run for the narrow alleyways. I nodded shakily as I unwillingly let my hand drop from Yuxin's.

The next thing I knew, we were sprinting in different directions. I could hear the men chasing after me as I crashed into the alleyway, running as fast as my legs could carry me while the sound of footsteps grew louder and louder.

Just before I reached the bustling street at the other end of the alley, a pair of rough hands closed around me. They yanked me backward as I kicked and thrashed. I tried to scream, but someone forced a sweet-smelling cloth over my mouth and nose. The scent filled my head as I struggled. My movements felt lethargic as it clouded my mind. And then the next thing I knew, the world faded to black.

Chapter Three

Sometimes, when I closed my eyes, I could still picture Yuxin's smiling face. I could still hear her voice in my dreams. But whenever I opened my eyes, she would be gone.

Even after all these years, I kept finding myself thinking back to that day. I still remembered the roughness of the rope that bound my hands. I still remembered the way it dug into my skin as I desperately scanned the faces of the other terrified girls in the wagon with me only to find that Yuxin was not among them.

I sat in front of a small mirror, running my fingers over a wooden comb in my hand. The red marks from the rope had long faded from my wrists.

"Xiyan," a voice said softly. I hastily reached up to wipe the tears stinging my eyes, turned away from the mirror, and smiled up at the girl standing in front of me. "Xiyan!" Her eyes instantly filled with concern. "Are you alright? Is something wrong?"

I smiled even as I sniffled. "I'm fine, Weiwei."

Weiwei shook her head as she took a seat on the bench next to me. "I can tell you're not fine. You're thinking about your sister, aren't you."

"I just don't know how she's doing out there." I could feel the sadness as it tightened around my heart. I turned to look out the window. The branches of the trees outside were swaying lightly in the wind. The sun had just begun to rise, and the sky was still colored with hues of the night.

Weiwei gently pried the comb from my hands. "I'll help you with your hair."

I sat quietly as she braided and tied up my hair. In the mirror, I watched as the other young women in the room began to wake. They shuffled around, talking quietly among themselves as they changed out of their nightgowns. I had already changed into my maid's uniform, and the fabric was soft against my skin.

Weiwei finished my hair, then leaned over my shoulder to offer me a smile in the copper mirror.

One of the other young women came over to us. "Hu Qiuwei, Xia Xiyan, remember, the two of you are responsible for serving the princess's guests today."

Weiwei offered the woman a reassuring smile. "We know, Sister Sun. Once they arrive at noon, we'll break from our regular duties to attend to them."

The young woman nodded before walking away.

I sighed once she was out of earshot. Out of all of us in this room, Sun Xiaoting was the oldest of us palace maids. And even though she was a maid just like the rest of us, she was the one who kept us on top of our work.

"Come on"-Weiwei pulled me to my feet-"we've got ten minutes until we go to the kitchens for breakfast."

"Weiwei," I sniffled. "Will I ever see my sister again?"

"Of course you'll see her again," Weiwei said softly. "You just need to survive the palace long enough to get out."

"I've been here for seven years now," I said sadly as I let her lead me out the door. I fixed my composure the moment we crossed the threshold, and I lowered my voice. "You've been here even longer."

"It's not that bad here, though," Weiwei tried. "If we just keep our heads down, we get food and shelter and-"

"But at what cost?" I asked tiredly. "If we had a choice, neither of us would be here in the palace, wasting away our lives in servitude."

Weiwei dropped her gaze. "I know you got a short taste of freedom, but I never got to experience it at all. My father sold me himself. For me, this is a second chance at life."

"But have you ever wondered if there's something more to life than this?"

"Xiyan, we've gone over this before. This is life."

"Haven't you ever dreamed of falling in love?" I asked wistfully as I looked up at the sky. The vast canvas was now painted in pink and orange from the sunrise, and the palace walls glowed golden in the light. "Have you ever dreamed of being able to live for yourself?"

"I have. But to keep longing for what you don't have will just make you miserable."

"You say that, but I get the feeling you dream anyway."

After the two of us finished our breakfast in the kitchen, we spent the majority of the morning on our knees, scrubbing the wooden steps and railings of one of the palace's many courtyards.

When noon came around, the two of us separated from the other maids to meet the princess's guests.

The first young woman who was helped out of her carriage was dressed in purple. She held a fan in one hand and a box in the other. As she marched to the palace doors, the young woman unapologetically shoved the box into my arms and, without a second glance in my direction, brushed past me to step inside. I resisted the urge to grimace as I turned to follow her. Weiwei was left to help the second young woman now climbing out of the carriage.

I silently followed the woman through the palace, and when we finally reached the princess's courtyard, there was a loud shriek as the doors to the princess's room flew open. The princess came flying out in a flurry of flowing red sleeves and skirts. Her maids trailed after her, noticeably flustered, until she skidded to a stop in front of the young woman in purple.

Even though the princess couldn't be older than Weiwei and me, her demeanor was that of a girl much younger. As the emperor's youngest child and only daughter, the princess was spoiled to the point where what little manners she once possessed vanished entirely. The princess's eyes immediately fell on the box in my hands, and she squealed in delight. "Is this a present for me?"

The young woman in the purple smiled politely. "I had this specially prepared for you, Your Highness. I hope Your Highness will like it."

Knowing that was my cue, I stepped forward and held out the box to the princess. The princess eagerly snatched the box from me and flung open the lid. With my head bent down, I couldn't see what the gift was, but from the way the princess was giggling in delight, it must have pleased her. Then she paused. "Where's your older sister? I thought she was coming with you."

"I'm here, I'm here," a voice called from behind us, and a young woman dressed in blue glided forward.

"Hurry, hurry!" the princess said excitedly. "Do you have a present for me too?"

Weiwei stepped forward, bowing as she presented a second box to the princess. Once the princess snatched the box from her, Weiwei stepped back to stand behind the woman in blue.

"The two of you know me the best!" the princess said confidently after she closed the second box. "Come on, let's go to my garden. There's tea and desserts prepared."

"Did Your Highness only prepare one maid each for us?" the young woman in blue asked as we all walked toward the gardens.

"Of course not," the princess replied. "I've prepared your usual courtyard, complete with an entire staff of servants. After tea, I'll show you there myself."

The woman in purple elegantly lifted her gauzy fan above her nose and let out a small laugh. "There's no need for you to go yourself, Your Highness. We remember the way."

We reached the garden, and when the three noblewomen reached the pavilion in the center, they sat down and chatted for a long time. After pouring their tea, Weiwei and I stood off to the side with one of the princess's maids.

After a while, the princess turned to look at me. "You, maid. Follow me."

I hurried after the princess as she marched out of the pavilion.

"I want you to tell my nanny to arrange the guest courtyard for my friends. Oh, and tell her to send in the maids and servants to serve them."

"Yes, Your Highness." I bowed before hurrying off. Of course the princess had forgotten to prepare the courtyard.

By the time I returned to the pavilion, the sun was beginning to make its way toward the horizon. "I think it's about time we retired to our chambers," said the young woman in blue as she rose from her seat.

The princess nodded. "I think so too." Then she turned to Weiwei and me. "Show them the way."

Weiwei and I curtsied to the princess before leading the two noblewomen out of the gardens. Once we had left the princess's wing, the two noblewomen immediately started talking. "I can't believe we wasted the entire afternoon accompanying the princess," the woman in purple scoffed. "I get a headache whenever she opens her mouth."

"It's a good thing we had some extra jewelry in the manor," the woman in blue added. "Otherwise what would we look like if we showed up to the palace empty-handed?"

The woman in purple laughed. "And the princess said she liked them. I can't believe she actually thinks we came here for her."

I exchanged a glance with Weiwei as the two noblewomen brushed past us and into the guest courtyard. What I had gotten from their conversation with the princess was that these two noblewomen were sisters, and the one in blue was the elder one. Li was their family name, and the young woman whom I was trailing was named Li Qinghua.

After the two noblewomen entered the room at the back of the courtyard, Weiwei and I helped them change out of their intricately embroidered dresses and into their nightgowns. All the luggage they brought had been dropped off and unpacked by the other maids already. I skillfully pulled out all of the golden hairpins adorning Li Qinghua's hair. After brushing it out, Weiwei and I silently curtsied to them before leaving the room and shutting the doors behind us.

Just as we stepped outside, another maid hurried over to us. It was Sun Xiaoting, and she asked us to follow her down the wooden steps. Once we were a good distance from the room, Sun Xiaoting spoke quietly. "There's been a new arrangement. All the maids in our room are to come to the guest wing every day to serve the Li sisters. The two of you will only need to be their personal maids for another day or so until their own maids arrive with the rest of their luggage."

"How long are they staying?" I asked quietly.

"Two months," Sun Xiaoting answered.

"Two months?" Weiwei echoed.

Sun Xiaoting sighed as she led us out of the courtyard and back toward our quarters. "Their father is a famous general, and now that he's going to lead soldiers out of the capital, it only makes sense for them to come here. The sisters are candidates for potential brides for the princes, after all."

When we arrived back at the maid quarters, I flopped face-first onto the long stretch of wood pressed against the side of the room, which served as our shared bed. Weiwei took a seat next to me as she began to undo the braids in my hair.

There was soft chatter as the maids talked among themselves. Once everyone had returned to the room, Sun Xiaoting made her rounds, instructing everyone to go to bed.

I flipped onto my back and stared up at the ceiling. Our normal routine of keeping the palace in order beat following the Li sisters around all day. At least when I was cleaning, Weiwei and I could chat together in lowered voices. Our normal routine allowed us to avoid the royals in the palace, but now that the sisters were here, it seemed like we would be seeing the princess a lot more. And spending too much time near any members of the imperial family wasn't exactly a good thing. But I knew my opinion didn't matter.

A few years ago, a maid had a very close relationship with one of the princes. At the time, I would often overhear gossip about how the prince favored the young maid. But then the maid became pregnant, and shortly after the news spread around the palace, she vanished, never to be seen again.

And then there was that one incident where the Crown Prince's wife-the princess consort-accused her husband of having an affair with a maid behind her back. The Crown Prince denied his wife's accusations, but all of the maids serving the eastern palace were then switched out by the princess consort and sent to the mines as slaves. To this day, no one knew what the truth was.

I turned over in bed as my stomach let out a rumble. I had missed dinner. I shut my eyes. Tomorrow was going to be another long day.

When I awoke in the morning, I sat by the mirror at the back of the room as I tied up my hair. The sky outside the window was still dark, and our room was still bathed in darkness. After breakfast, Weiwei and I headed to the guest's wing with breakfast for the Li sisters.

When they finally woke up, I helped comb and pin up Li Qinghua's hair while Weiwei did Li Qingmei's. After the sisters finished dressing, Weiwei and I trailed them around the courtyard gardens. The blooming flowers were a burst of color in the otherwise lifeless palace. We followed them along the wooden bridges over the pond that glittered in the sunlight. Aside from the sisters' chatter, the air was still and quiet.

Around late morning, a maid I didn't recognize walked over to the sisters. "The princess wishes to see you in her residence," she announced.

"The princess?" Li Qingmei echoed distastefully as she set down her teacup.

Li Qinghua didn't even bother to hide her frown behind her gauzy purple fan. "How annoying." With that said, the Li sisters exchanged a glance before rising from their seats.

When we arrived at the princess's wing, the princess herself came running out of her room. Today she was dressed in pink, and the long fabric of her skirts fluttered in the spring breeze. "Qingmei, Qinghua, you're here!" she called excitedly.

"We came as soon as Your Highness called," Li Qinghua said with a polite smile.

"Exactly." Li Qingmei dipped her head in agreement. "We're the best of sisters. How could we not come immediately?"

"I'm lucky to have such great sisters!" the princess grinned from ear to ear. "Come on, let's go do something fun." But just then, the princess froze as her eyes landed on something behind us. "Brother! What are you doing here?"

The other maids and I quickly dropped our head and sank into deep curtsies. Even after I rose, I kept my head bent and my eyes on the ground.

"Eldest Lady Li," the third prince acknowledged the Li sisters. "Second Lady Li."

"Your Highness," the sisters chorused.

Out of the corner of my eye, I glanced at the prince. I had only seen him in person a handful of times before. He was tall and at least ten years older than the princess.

"What are you doing here?" the princess asked again, annoyed by her brother's arrival.

"I heard that General Li's daughters arrived at the palace," the third prince explained smoothly. "I wanted to go greet them, but when I arrived at the guest wing, they had already gone to see you, my dear sister."

The princess huffed. "You're ruining our fun. Leave!"

Li Qingmei turned to the princess with a faint smile. "We don't mind the third prince's company."

"His Highness came all the way here, after all," Li Qinghua added. "It would be rude to send His Highness away like that."

"At least some of you are sensible," the prince chuckled as he ignored his sister. "I can't stay for long, though. I'm here on behalf of the other princes. They send their greetings."

"Will you not accompany us for tea?" Li Qinghua asked in dismay.

"How about this," the prince said. "I'll stay and drink a cup with the three of you. Then I really shouldn't delay much longer."

The prince strolled forward despite the princess's protests. The Li sisters exchanged an excited look before they quickly followed him. Weiwei and I trailed after them, and the two of us were accompanied by other maids and bodyguards.

"It's rare for me to have friends over," the princess said angrily when they all arrived at the pavilion. "Can't you leave them to me?"

When the prince continued to ignore her, the princess snatched the teacup from him and flung it to the ground. The porcelain cup shattered on the stones. All the maids and bodyguards, including myself, instantly dropped to the floor and pressed our heads to the stones.

"Your Highness!" the princess's maids piped fearfully. "Please calm down!"

"I will not calm down!" the princess said shrilly. "I told my third brother that he's not allowed anywhere near my courtyard, and yet now he's here!"

"My dear sister, I-" the prince started with a sigh.

"I don't want to hear it!" the princess snapped. "You caused me to lose my favorite maid!"

"Is this what you're mad about?" The third prince laughed, but there was something almost nervous in the sound. "Dear sister, you've got plenty of new maids." Then the prince glanced at us. "I think the princess is tired. See her to her room to rest, will you? And someone clean up these shards."

Weiwei and I were there in an instant as we swiftly collected the fragments.

The third prince turned back to the Li sisters as the fuming princess was ushered from the pavilion. "I'm sorry you had to see such an argument between siblings." He picked up the new teacup that one of his servants had poured for him and drank deeply.

"It's fine." Li Qinghua smiled faintly. "It's only natural for siblings to argue."

After spending some time politely chatting, the third prince rose from his seat, bid his farewell to the Li sisters, and took his leave. As Weiwei and I trailed the sisters back to the guest wing, the two of them remained silent until they were back in their room.

"His Highness actually came to see us!" Li Qingmei squealed after Weiwei had shut the door behind the sisters. "The third prince actually came to see us! Did you see the way he looked at me? The next thing you know, I'm going to be his wife!"

"Is something wrong with your brain?" Li Qinghua scoffed as she took a seat at the table in front of the window. She fanned herself lightly with her purple fan. "Who wants to be the third prince's wife?"

Li Qingmei stared at her sister for a moment before hurrying over to take the chair across from her. Her blue skirts fluttered in her wake. "But he's the most handsome of all the princes."

Li Qinghua set her fan down on the table. "He's the most impulsive of all the princes. He may seem polite on the outside, but the third prince will do anything to get his hands on what he thinks is his. All of that would be fine if he knew how to lie low. But he's an idiot and is constantly being manipulated by the people around him. Once he gets bold enough to fight the Crown Prince for the throne, it won't end well for him or anyone close to him. If you want to marry any of the princes, it should be the second prince. Even though he isn't as good-looking as his third brother, he's sly and cunning. If anyone can take down the Crown Prince, it will be him. And then, as his wife, you'll be the new princess consort."

"What about you?" Li Qingmei asked. "Who do you have your eyes on?"

"Me?" Li Qinghua said smugly. "I've got my eyes on the sixth prince."

Li Qingmei wrinkled her nose. "What's so good about the sixth prince?"

"What isn't there to like? He's the second most handsome of the princes, and he knows how to stay out of trouble. If I become his wife, I'll be able to live a comfortable life in the palace without worrying about getting caught up in the older princes' power struggle."

"You're right! Of course my dear little sister always has the best foresight."

Suddenly, I let out a soft hiss as pain blossomed through my finger. I had unconsciously slipped my hand over my waistband only to remember I stashed the fragments of the broken tea cup there. I quickly withdrew my finger, but I was already bleeding.

The Li sisters' heads snapped up to look at me, and Li Qinghua let out a shriek. "Blood!"

"Get her out of here!" Li Qingmei demanded shrilly.

Weiwei was at my side in an instant, and the two of us hurried out of the room.

"Are you alright?" Weiwei took my hand in her own and examined my bleeding finger with worried eyes.

"I just wasn't careful and cut myself on the broken shards." I tried to offer Weiwei a smile, but I found myself tearing up from the stinging. "It hurts."

"Let's find you a bandage." Weiwei glanced over her shoulder at the sister's room before motioning me to follow her.

I shook my head as I trailed after her. "It's just a small cut. There's no need for bandages-just cleaning it will be fine."

"Come on," Weiwei said quietly. "Let's dispose of the rest of the shards."

After the two of us returned to our room, Weiwei prepared a bowl of water to wash my cut. I hissed softly as the water stung the wound. Weiwei helped me dry my hands with a clean cloth. When she was done, I walked over to the window, pushed it open, and rested my chin on my palms as I stared up at the blue sky.

The human realm wasn't supposed to be like this. Why was there always so much pain and pettiness? Where were the brave and fearless heroes I read about in the library back in the demon realm? I absently watched the leaves of the tree outside the room sway as a gentle breeze picked up. The fabric of my sleeves fluttered in and out of my vision, and I found myself recalling the martial artist I had met all those years ago.

"What are you thinking about?" Weiwei asked softly as she joined me at the window.

I dropped my gaze from the sky to look at my friend. "Why do humans have to be this way?"

"What way?"

I sniffed. "Why do I have to feel pain when I cut myself?"

Weiwei smiled gently as I rested my head on her shoulder. "All humans feel pain. It means we're alive."

I shook my head. "But I don't like it."

Weiwei just patted my head sympathetically. "Come on, we've got to go back to serve the Li sisters."

"How many more days until their own maids get here? The way they talk makes my head want to explode. Why are they thinking about marrying into the imperial family? They should be trying to run as far away from the palace as they can get. They're not trapped inside its walls yet."

"They don't want freedom," Weiwei said lightly. "They want the riches the palace has to offer."

"But what's wrong with living a simple life? What's wrong with finding joy in the simple things?"

"Some people will never feel satisfied with simple things, Xiyan."

I sighed as the two of us left our room and began the long walk back to the guest wing and the Li sisters.

✦ ✦ ✦

The following morning, I found out with much dismay that the Li sisters' maids still hadn't arrived. According to a messenger, they had been delayed and would arrive sometime in the late afternoon.

And so Weiwei and I were back in the sisters' room. We stood off to the side as the two of them gossiped about the princes.

"I think we have a very good chance of becoming the wife of one of the princes," Li Qinghua was saying. "The emperor himself has invited Father to the palace many times before. I think His Majesty wants to connect our families-then he'll have Father's military power at his beck and call."

"You want to marry the sixth prince," Li Qingmei said slowly. "But how do you plan to make him fall in love with you? He's the one that will need to propose to you, after all."

Li Qinghua gave her sister a smug smile. "I have my ways."

"But what about you?" Li Qingmei asked. "You don't love the sixth prince."

Li Qinghua fanned herself with her fan. "Marriage is never about love. Love comes after marriage. I'm sure after we've become husband and wife, the sixth prince will come to love me."

After a long pause, Li Qingmei changed the topic. "I heard that a famine just hit the western part of the kingdom. Father's going to be passing through there. Do you think he'll be alright?"

"A famine?" Li Qinghua blinked. "How could there be a famine? We've got plenty of food to eat."

"The people in the western part of the kingdom don't, though."

"Well, if they don't have food, can't they just go buy some?" Li Qinghua asked impatiently. "All those commoners need to learn how to solve their own problems. They can't always come to us to fix all their problems for them, can they?"

Li Qingmei frowned for a moment before shrugging. "You have a point." Then she changed the topic again. "Did you hear about Young Master Wen?"

"What about him?" Li Qinghua asked, uninterested.

"My cousin sent me a letter filling me in on the latest gossip," Li Qingmei said dramatically. "Young Master Wen and his wife died! The family covered it up for an entire year, but it's finally coming out that they died horrible deaths on the same day. They were poisoned!"

Before her sister could respond, a maid came hurrying into the room. "Eldest Lady Li, Second Lady Li." She bowed to the sisters. "The rest of your luggage and personal maids have arrived in front of the palace."

"Finally!" Li Qingmei rose from her seat. "I need to go check if all my jewelry got here safe and sound."

"And my dresses!" Li Qinghua hurried after her sister as they followed the maid out of the room.

Weiwei and I made to follow them, but Li Qinghua paused as she turned to face the two of us. "You maids, clear some room for our belongings before we get back!"

"Yes, milady." Weiwei and I both curtsied.

The two of us folded the clothes and picked up the accessories the sisters had flung over the tables and floors. Weiwei got to work hanging up the variously colored silk scarves while I made a pile of clothing that needed to be washed, fearing that the sisters would complain later. It was easy to distinguish Li Qingmei's clothing from Li Qinghua's; each sister used a different floral fragrance that clung to their clothing and everything they touched.

After carefully balancing the two stacks in my arms, I pushed open the door with my foot and made my way out into the courtyard. The warmth of the sun beat down on me as I walked down the stone path. It was late morning now, and even though the palace was busy at this time, the guest courtyard was still and silent.

Suddenly, the sound of hurried footsteps echoed down the path. I tried to look over the tower of laundry obscuring my vision, but before I could determine where the footsteps were coming from or who they belonged to, something crashed into me, and I toppled backward.

Chapter Four

I yelped as I hit the ground, instinctively curling up from the impact. My head spun, and I realized with a sinking feeling that my pile of laundry was no longer in my arms. Someone let out a soft groan next to me. I blinked as I quickly sat up. A young man around my age was lying on the grass, and an overturned basket of flowers lay next to him.

I sneezed as flowers drifted down onto the grass around us. My concern for the laundry vanished immediately. "Are you alright?" I asked in a panic as I turned to look at the young man. "I'm so sorry! I couldn't see where I was going-"

"No, this was my fault." The young man slowly sat up and winced as he clapped a hand to his head. When he saw me, he clapped his hands over his face in embarrassment. Suddenly, the wind picked up, and the flowers spilling out of his overturned basket took flight. "The flowers!" he cried as he frantically scrambled to scoop them back into the basket.

I was there at his side in an instant. We hastily crawled around, collecting the rest of the scattered flowers before the wind could carry them away.

"Are you alright?" I asked again once all the flowers were back in the basket.

"I'm fine. W-what about you?" the young man stammered.

"I'm fine," I reassured him as I climbed to my feet. I brushed grass from my skirts before offering him a hand. After hesitating for a moment, he let me help him to his feet. It was only now that we were both standing that I realized the young man was dressed in the outfit of a servant. He was thin, with dirt caked on the hems of his clothes and grass caught in his dark hair.

"I'm a gardener here," he explained, then quickly dropped his gaze. "This is only my second day working in the guest courtyard. Normally I work on the other side of the palace."

"I normally don't work here either." I got to work collecting my scattered laundry. The gardener set his basket down to help me, and before long, my pile of clothes towered just as tall as it had before.

"Once I was alerted that the Li sisters left their room, I was told to go and change out their flower arrangements," the gardener said with a sigh as some of his initial timidness faded. "The two of us better hurry before they get back."

I nodded in agreement and turned to continue on my way down the path. "Good luck, then." I had only traveled a few paces before I found myself turning back around. "Wait! My name's Xia Xiyan. What's your name?" The wind had picked up again, and I had to squint to see him through the fluttering of the gauzy fabric in my arms.

The gardener turned to look at me over his shoulder, surprised. "My name's Shen Fanghuan."

"Xiyan?" Weiwei emerged from the room behind the gardener. "I heard voices."

"Gardener Shen and I accidentally bumped into each other," I explained with an embarrassed smile.

"You need to be more careful, Xiyan," Weiwei scolded as she walked over to me. She took half the stack of laundry from me. "Let's go together."

I nodded my head as the two of us started down the stone path. I glanced back over my shoulder to watch Shen Fanghuan step through the doors. But before he vanished, he, too, looked back at me. I flashed him a bright smile as his eyes met mine, and the gardener's face turned red before he quickly ducked inside.

✦ ✦ ✦

The next few days went by much more smoothly than the previous ones. Now that the Li sisters had their maids to follow them around, Weiwei and I were free of that task. We were now responsible for helping the other maids keep the guest wing tidy. Whenever the sisters walked through the courtyard, we would all do our best to avoid them. And when the sisters left to visit the princess, only then would we enter their room to clean.

"Weiwei," I said absently as the two of us swept leaves off the stone path in the corner of the courtyard. "What do you think's beyond these walls?"

"The world, of course," Weiwei said simply.

I paused my sweeping to tip my head back and look up at the high stone walls surrounding the courtyard. I could see the blue sky, but it was always so far out of reach. "My sister's out there somewhere."

Weiwei sighed. "I know. If we can ever figure out how to leave this place, I promise I'll help you find her."

I broke into a smile, and Weiwei smiled back.

✦ ✦ ✦

"What are you waiting for?" Li Qinghua's distant voice demanded. "Kneel, all of you!"

Weiwei and I were washing the wooden deck. We exchanged a worried glance, silently communicating that we should see what was happening, so we quietly made our way around the corner.

"You two!" Li Qingmei's gaze snapped up to us from where she was standing next to her sister. "Get over here and kneel."

Horrified, Weiwei and I scurried over to where a number of the sisters' maids were groveling on the ground in front of them. Weiwei and I dropped down beside them and bowed until our heads touched the stone.

"Milady"-one of the maids lifted her head-"please calm down! The princes only didn't talk to the two of you today because they were in a rush-"

"Silence!" Li Qinghua snapped as she slapped the maid across the face.
