"Who knocked you out?" Weiwei asked.

The shop owner just looked at us blankly. "Who are you?"

"That's not important," Yuxin said. "Who knocked you out?"

The shop owner frowned as he clapped a hand to his head. "There were at least two of them. They just appeared. I asked them what they wanted to buy, and the next thing I know, I'm waking up on the floor."

"What did they look like?" I pushed.

"They were martial artists," the owner recalled as he furrowed his brow. "They were dressed in the colors of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect."

My heart sank. We should have gone into the shop with Yao Jie. If we had just been there-

"If we entered the shop with him," Weiwei said quietly as if she could read my thoughts, "we might have lost our lives too."

"But-" my voice broke. "But Yao Jie might not have died either."

"Someone died?" the shop owner asked, horrified.

I just let out a sob.

✦ ✦ ✦

By the time we returned to Chen Han's residence, my eyes were puffy from crying. Yuxin's face was paler than usual, and Weiwei had silent tears streaming down her own face. The Fire Sea Abyss Sect had gone too far.

I stopped in front of the room Tian Yong was staying in and shakily knocked on the door.

"Come in," Tian Yong's voice called from inside.

I silently stepped into the room, with Weiwei and Yuxin close at my heel. I set the box of desserts down next to Tian Yong. "I-" I started, but my words seemed to get stuck in my throat.

Tian Yong didn't seem to notice my hesitation as he expectantly opened the box. As he looked at the dessert cakes inside, his face split into a grin. "Did Yao Jie buy these? I didn't know he remembered I liked them."

"Yao Jie bought them," I whispered. "But he's-he's-"

Tian Yong looked over at us, and his expression instantly turned worried. "What happened to Yao Jie?"

"He was murdered," Yuxin said gravely.

Tian Yong just stared at us. "You're joking."

"I'm sorry, Tian Yong," Weiwei said regretfully. "Yao Jie was killed by members of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect."

Tian Yong's face had completely drained of all color.

I closed my eyes briefly as I tried to center myself. "It's our fault. If only we had gone with him, if only we had taken Sister Chen with us, then maybe-maybe this wouldn't have happened."

A deafening silence filled the room. Then Tian Yong quickly climbed to his feet, but his injured leg gave out from beneath him.

"Tian Yong!" I was there in an instant as I tried to steady him. "Your leg's still injured!"

"They just killed my friend!" Tian Yong yelled as he tried to push me away. "I need to avenge him!"

"Please calm down!" Yuxin hurried forward. "You're going to hurt yourself!"

Tian Yong continued to struggle. "I don't care. My friend's dead!"

Weiwei raised her voice. "If you hurt yourself, how are you going to avenge him?"

At that, Tian Yong paused. He sat back down on his bed and pressed his hands over his face. "I can't believe it. Yao Jie was fine this morning."

"His murderers took his jade pendant," I said quietly.

Tian Yong looked up at me, and his eyes were hopeless. "I need to avenge Yao Jie. I need to find his jade pendant. Where's his body now?"

"The owner of the shop Yao Jie died in felt bad," Weiwei explained sadly. "He told us that he's always had great respect for the Owl and Aspen Sect and would help take care of Yao Jie's burial."

Tian Yong just stared blankly the box of dessert cakes, and his shoulders slumped in defeat.

"We'll give you some time alone," I said softly. I motioned for Weiwei and Yuxin to follow me out of the room. As I closed the door behind us, I turned around to find myself face-to-face with Chen Han.

"I heard everything," the heroine in red said solemnly. There was a sadness flickering behind her eyes. "I thought that by beating up those members of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect, they would have left and gone back to their headquarters. I never would have thought that they'd stick around and retaliate by killing Yao Jie."

"Why didn't you kill them?" Yuxin turned to Chen Han in distress. "If you had just killed them, Yao Jie wouldn't have died!"

Chen Han's eyes blazed. "Killing people isn't something one should take lightly."

"He was our friend and we let him down-"

"Enough," Chen Han said firmly.

Yuxin fell silent at that.

In an attempt to break the rising tension, Weiwei asked, "Is there liquor?"

Chen Han blinked. "Liquor? What-yes, of course. This way."

I spent the rest of the day sitting alone on the front porch with my knees drawn to my chest. I couldn't do anything except stare blankly at the grass.

Weiwei, Yuxin, and Chen Han spent the rest of the daylight hours drinking before finally parting ways. As night fell, I took it upon myself to check on Tian Yong and bring him something to eat. When I entered the room, I found him still sitting on the bed just as he had been when we left him.

"Are you alright?" I asked softly as I stood in the doorway.

Tian Yong raised his head. His eyes were red. "Do you think you could sit here with me?"

I nodded and silently made my way over to him. After setting the tray I brought with me off to the side, I offered him a bowl of soup. I placed a comforting hand on his shoulder as he shakily lifted the bowl to his mouth, and the two of us sat there in silence as the flames of the dying candles slowly flickered out.

✦ ✦ ✦

When I returned to the room I shared with Weiwei and Yuxin, I found it unoccupied.

I awoke in the morning to the sound of someone shuffling around the room. I sat up and rubbed the sleep from my eyes, looking around to find Weiwei frantically searching through all the drawers. "Weiwei? What are you looking for?"

Weiwei whirled around in alarm at the sound of my voice. "Letters," she gasped out.

I just looked at her in confusion. "Letters?"

"Did you see the letters I put here?" Weiwei asked in a rising panic.

I shook my head, bewildered.

Weiwei clapped a hand to her head. "Did I leave them in the study? But I already checked there. I can't remember where I put my letters. I-I seem to have been too drunk to remember."

I sighed. "Weiwei, you shouldn't have been drinking that much. Who are you writing to anyway? Here, I'll help you look."

"Don't!" Weiwei said quickly. "There's no point now. They've vanished."

There was a shuffling outside the door, and it slid open a moment later to reveal Yuxin.

"Have you seen Weiwei's letters?" I asked.

Yuxin just blinked. "Letters? What letters?"

Weiwei shook her head. "It doesn't matter. Maybe I was the one who threw them out."

✦ ✦ ✦

Over the next week, Yuxin's presence at the residence was scarce. When I wasn't practicing martial arts, I spent most of my time helping out with the cooking and cleaning. Something about the atmosphere was different than before. Even when I went to buy us meat and vegetables, the bustle in the town no longer seemed as lively as I remembered.

As I neared the center of the town, I spotted a group of people all gathered around a particular vendor. Curious about what was so popular, I made my way over to them.

"Selling paper talismans!" the vendor called as he waved them in the air. "Protect yourselves and your families from ghosts!"

"I think we should buy as many as we can," the woman standing in front of me was telling her friend. "Even those martial artists from the Fire Sea Abyss Sect weren't able to defend themselves."

"You can't be serious," the woman's friend said in shock. "But they're martial artists!"

The first woman lowered her voice, and I had to lean forward to try and catch her words. "I heard it was horrible," she said. "Here, here, and here"-she gestured to her throat and wrists-"they were punctured straight through and left bleeding out. Not only that, but their faces were also grotesquely disfigured. If not a ghost, what else would do such a thing?"

I silently slipped away from the crowd. When I returned to Chen Han's residence, I absently got to work stocking our pantry. That night, I was sitting around the table eating dinner with Chen Han, Weiwei, and Tian Yong. When we were halfway through our meal, Yuxin stepped into the room.

The moment she appeared, Chen Han rose to her feet and strode across the room until she was right in front of Yuxin. My mouth fell open in shock as the heroine in red slapped Yuxin across the face.

Yuxin staggered in surprise. She slowly lifted her hand to the side of her face, hurt flashing in her eyes as she looked at Chen Han.

"Kneel," Chen Han said heavily as she pointed to the yard outside. "I want you to kneel. You've gone against my teachings, and if you still acknowledge me as your teacher, you're not allowed to rise until I say so."

Tian Yong looked back and forth between them in confusion. "I-what's going on?"

Chen Han pointed her finger at Yuxin. "She hunted down and killed those members of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect responsible for Yao Jie's death. That was foolish. If they link the murders back to you, you've just made yourself and everyone else in this residence a target! And if they decide that it was the Owl and Aspen Sect who did the killing, you could start a sect war! Do you know how many people will die then?"

A tear slid down the side of Yuxin's cheek. "Yao Jie was wronged. Is wanting to avenge him wrong?"

"Go outside and kneel."

With one last pained glance at the heroine in red, Yuxin turned on her heel and silently left the room. Even late at night when Weiwei and I returned to our room, we paused on the balcony to look out at the yard to find Yuxin still kneeling in the dark.

✦ ✦ ✦

Fei Ziyi returned within the next week, and Chen Han filled him in on everything that had happened during his absence. As we expected, he was horrified to hear about Yao Jie's death and the Fire Sea Abyss Sect. He seemed ready to storm the Fire Sea Abyss Sect himself, and it took us a good hour to talk him out of it.

By the time Tian Yong's leg healed completely, winter had arrived, and snow painted the world in white. The six of us walked in silence as Tian Yong somberly led the way toward the Owl and Aspen Sect. I wasn't sure how many days had passed until we finally arrived at the main hall of the Owl and Aspen Sect. But as we drew near the front doors, it quickly became apparent to us that something was off.

Tian Yong, who had been leading the group, threw out a hand and stopped us in our tracks. "Something's wrong," he said softly. "Usually, there's people standing guard here." Tian Yong dropped his gaze to the stone steps. I inhaled sharply as my eyes fell on what he was looking at. Blood. There was dried blood crusted on the stones.

Chen Han stepped to the front of the group, sword in hand. As we walked through the entrance, an eerie silence engulfed us. I could hear my heart thundering away in my chest, but as I strained my ears for any sounds of life, I couldn't hear anything at all.

As I dropped my eyes to the stone path, I nearly let out a cry when I realized with a start that, it, too was splattered with blood.

"Well, if it isn't Master Wu's disciples," an amused voice called. The sound sliced through the silence like a knife. A man in his early forties appeared on the path in front of us. He was dressed in fiery orange robes, and his hands were lazily clasped behind his back.

Chen Han smiled a smile that didn't quite reach her eyes. "Master Huang. You still haven't apologized for my master's death."

Master Huang just smiled back. "Is that so? I don't remember Wu Ren's death having anything to do with me."

Fei Ziyi drew his sword. "The Ivory Snow sect spread rumors that my master had decided to fight for them," he said. "You could have called off your elite disciples from chasing him down. But you saw him as competition, so you were happy to let him die."

"You have no proof of what you say," Master Huang said lightly. "I'd advise you not to slander me, especially here in the midst of my sect members."

"The Fire Sea Abyss Sect is here?" Tian Yong demanded. "Just what in the name of hell did you do to my Owl and Aspen Sect?"

Master Huang shrugged. "I'm eliminating my competition. I gave the birds here a choice: they could either join my Fire Sea Abyss Sect or die."

Tian Yong's eyes blazed. "You-"

"Master Huang," Fei Ziyi said darkly, "don't believe we won't take your life right now."

Master Huang just chuckled. "You and your senior? I'd like to see the two of you try. Fei Ziyi, if I didn't know any better, I'd think you were a lazy playboy from the capital. What happened to the rising young martial artist you were the last time I saw you? And Chen Han, you've fallen from your prime as well. Neither of you is worthy to be my opponent."

"Where are my fellow sect members?" Tian Yong's voice was deadly calm.

"You're from the Owl and Aspen Sect?" Master Huang's eyes drifted over to Tian Yong. "You came just in time then. Follow me." With that said, Master Huang turned on his heel and made his way toward another set of double doors on the other side of the hall.

Master Huang carelessly pushed open the doors to the next courtyard. I nearly jumped back in horror at the scene in front of us. Nearly a hundred people sat in the middle of the courtyard with their hands and feet bound. All of them were around my age and they wore the tawny brown robes of the Owl and Aspen Sect. But standing in a circle around them were figures dressed in the orange robes of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect.

"Where's my master?" Tian Yong asked, his face paling.

"Master Zeng?" Master Huang said mildly. "I've got him locked up in his study."

"Tian Yong?" a voice called from the midst of the Owl and Aspen Sect members. "Tian Yong, run while you still can!"

Tian Yong desperately turned to Master Huang. "Let them go! Please, I'm begging you!"

"They refuse to join me," Master Huang said. "They're too loyal to Master Zeng for their own good."

"I won't join you either," Tian Yong said coldly.

Master Huang just shrugged. "That's fine. I don't need an angry boy like you in my sect." Master Huang raised a hand, and two members from the Fire Sea Abyss Sect instantly sprung forward. In seconds, they tied Tian Yong's together, then dragged him to the circle and forced him to his knees alongside the other Owl and Aspen Sect members.

Master Huang turned to Chen Han and Fei Ziyi. "What about you? The two of you have come all the way here. Why not join my Fire Sea Abyss Sect?" Then his gaze flicked over Weiwei, Yuxin, and me. "What about these three? Who are they?"

"They're my students," Chen Han said coolly. "I'm not joining you, and you can't have my students either."

Master Huang let out a sigh. "I figured it'd be something like that. Capture them."

Almost immediately, a number of Fire Sea Abyss members swooped forward. Chen Han and Fei Ziyi had their swords out, and metal blurred as they fought off their attackers. Weiwei, Yuxin, and I had our swords out as well, but there was only so much fighting we could do before we were forced to surrender.

As I watched Chen Han and Fei Ziyi continue to fight off the Fire Sea Abyss Sect members, a sinking feeling began to seep through me. There was something unusual about the way Chen Han was fighting. Her movements were growing slower, and whenever she spun around, she'd momentarily freeze as if she was disoriented. And then the heroine in red fell to the ground.

"Chen Han!" Fei Ziyi's head snapped around as Chen Han hit the floor. His own sword clattered to the ground as he dropped to his knees next to her. Fei Ziyi glared up at the Fire Sea Abyss Sect members as they all pointed their swords at the two of them. "What did you do to her?"

"We didn't even touch her!" one of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect members said defensively. "She just fell over!"

"Chen Han!" Fei Ziyi desperately tried to shake the heroine in red awake. "Chen Han, wake up!"

"Master, what should we do with them?" another one of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect members asked.

"We'll kill them too," Master Huang said, uninterested. "This way they won't get in our way again."

"Wait!" I said suddenly. Everyone turned to look at me, and I struggled to hold onto my confidence. "Master Huang-your northern accent!"

Master Huang blinked at me. "What about my accent?" Then he narrowed his eyes. "The only people who would recognize my accent are the ones from my hometown in the far north."

"I had a friend once with the same accent," I said quietly, still in a state of shock. "He worked as a gardener in the palace. When he spoke slowly, his accent was almost inaudible. But when he had a lot to say and spoke quickly, his accent would come out."

Master Huang just stared, his expression impassive. "What was his last name?"

"Shen."

"Shen," Master Huang echoed. "I knew Mrs. Shen."

"You knew his mother?" I asked in surprise.

"It's a small village," Master Huang said as he clasped his hands behind his back. "I knew everyone there." Then he turned to look at me. "What happened to her son?"

"He's dead," I whispered. A tear slid down the side of my face.

"Dead?" Master Huang staggered. Then his tone grew deadly calm. "Who killed Shen Fanghuan?"

I felt my heart rate increase. "I don't know. There was a martial artist sneaking around in the palace, though. People say he was a pirate. I-I think that pirate was somehow involved in his death."

Master Huang stared at me for a long moment before finally turning away. "Fire Sea Abyss Sect members, listen up. We're going to Jingcheng."

Chapter Nineteen

"Master," someone said, "we aren't killing the Owl and Aspen Sect members anymore?"

Master Huang shook his head. "Let them go. None of this matters anymore. I have some business I have to complete at the capital."

"Master Huang, wait!" I called as I was released by the Fire Sea Abyss member who had been holding my arms. "You and Mrs. Shen . . .?"

Master Huang paused at the doorway. "If Mr. Shen hadn't married her, I would have." And with that said, Master Huang stepped over the threshold and vanished into the mist.

✦ ✦ ✦

I stood outside the Owl and Aspen Sect's main hall with Weiwei and Yuxin. To my relief, Chen Han had regained consciousness and was now leaning against Fei Ziyi for support. Tian Yong stood in front of us, his eyes tired. "Miss Xia," he started. "Thanks to you, our sect members were spared. We're forever in your debt. If you ever need our help, all you have to do is ask."

"We just got lucky." I let out a shaky breath. "I just got lucky. His accent reminded me of someone I used to know."

"Tian Yong," Chen Han said. Her voice was weak. "What are you planning to do now?"

Determination sparked in Tian Yong's eyes. "I need to get justice for Yao Jie. I'm going to find his jade pendant and return it to him. Until we meet again." Tian Yong bowed to us for a final time before turning to help the other members of his sect.

"Let's get Sister Chen back home," Weiwei said quietly. "She's sick."

As we slowly made our way down the path, I looked over at the heroine in red in concern. "Why didn't you tell us you were sick?"

Chen Han coughed, and her voice was ragged when she spoke. "I thought if I gave it time, it would go away on its own. It seems like exerting myself just now made my condition take a turn for the worse."

"We need to get her to a doctor," Fei Ziyi said worriedly. "Hurry!"

Once we reached the nearest town and saw a doctor, he seemed to think that Chen Han's illness would subside with some time and rest. But upon returning to Chen Han's residence, the heroine in red hardly left her room. Fei Ziyi stayed by her side, while Weiwei, Yuxin, and I constantly visited.

I could feel my own worry beginning to sink in, and occasionally I found myself on the verge of a panic attack. I was scared. I didn't want to lose anyone else. Chen Han had to be alright.

I had hoped that Fei Ziyi's return would at least help Chen Han's insomnia, but it seemed I was hoping for too much. Chen Han hadn't gotten better; she had been progressively getting worse. But she hadn't told us. She hadn't even told Fei Ziyi.

Now with her makeup off, I could see just how sickly her complexion looked. One day, Weiwei and I were climbing up the stairs to deliver breakfast to Chen Han when suddenly we heard a loud thump. I exchanged a momentary glance with Weiwei before we rushed into her room.

The heroine in red had fallen out of her bed and was lying on the floor in a heap of crimson fabric. Fei Ziyi was already crouching next to her, trying to help Chen Han back to her feet.

"What happened?" I asked in a rising panic.

"She wanted to close the window," Fei Ziyi said as he cradled Chen Han's limp body in his arms. "But now she's too weak even to walk."

Weiwei's face paled. "Should we call the doctor here?"

Fei Ziyi's eyes were worried as he turned to Weiwei. "Can you do that?"

"I'll be back as soon as I can!" Weiwei said before dashing out of the room.

I let out a sob as Fei Ziyi gently laid Chen Han back down on the bed. "Sister Chen, please be alright!"

With much effort, Chen Han turned her head to look at me. She offered me a strained smile. "Maybe this is my fate."

"Your fate?" Fei Ziyi said in disbelief. "If this is fate, then screw fate! I refuse to believe this is how the fearless Chen Han will die. Why didn't you let me help you?"

Chen Han just shook her head tiredly. "I didn't even know I was this ill until I collapsed the other day." Suddenly, she began coughing violently.

Fei Ziyi quickly fumbled with the bottle of medicine the doctor had prescribed for Chen Han, but when he turned it upside down, nothing fell into his awaiting hand. "Xiyan!" Fei Ziyi looked over at me in a panic.

I felt myself begin to panic as well. "I'll go buy more medicine!" I swiftly hurried out of the room and down the stairs. In minutes, I was sprinting down the dirt path. Dark clouds were beginning to creep over the sky, and I gritted my teeth. Whether or not I'd be able to outrun the rain, I couldn't say.

By the time I skidded into the medicine shop, I was gasping for breath. I hurried over to the counter. With one hand, I clutched the stitch in my side, and with the other, I fumbled for a handful of coins. After collecting the medicine, I ran to the door of the shop only to run head-first into something very solid.

"Xiyan?" Yuxin's voice said in surprise.

My head snapped up. "Yuxin?"

Yuxin blinked at me. "I was just on the way back and heard your voice. What are you doing here?"

"Sister Chen ran out of medicine," I explained breathlessly. "I came here to get more. We can head back together."

The two of us rushed back down the dirt path, but in the end, we weren't fast enough to beat the rain. As the rain poured down around us, I sprinted through the mud. I blinked water out of my eyes as Chen Han's residence appeared in the distance. When I reached the front doors, I nearly collapsed against them, gasping for breath.

"Quick!" I pushed the bottle of medicine into Yuxin's hands. "Bring this to Sister Chen!"

Yuxin nodded once before hurrying into the yard.

I leaned against the wall next to the doors, clutching my chest. My heart was thundering, and I didn't realize I was violently shivering from the cold until I slumped down against the stones. I wrapped my arms tightly around myself. My clothes were completely waterlogged, and my teeth chattered in my skull. I squinted against the rain. Everything was blurring together. Drawing one uneven breath after another, the world turned sideways as I passed out.

✦ ✦ ✦

"Is she alright?" Weiwei's worried voice drew me awake.

"She's fine," an unfamiliar voice replied. "She's just had too much strain on her mind and body recently."

I blinked and the world slowly came into focus around me. I was lying in my makeshift bed. Weiwei's face was swimming in and out of view above me, and I winced as I slowly sat up. Yuxin stood next to Weiwei, and a middle-aged man stood next to her. It looked like the the doctor had been found after all.

"How's Sister Chen?" I whispered. My throat was hoarse.

"She's just taken her medicine," Weiwei answered quickly. Then she dropped to her knees beside me. "Xiyan, what happened? When I returned to the yard, you were lying outside in the rain."

"Yuxin and I ran back as quickly as we could with the medicine," I explained as pain shot through my head. "I ran the entire way there and back. I think I exhausted myself."

"Let's get you a bath and a change of clothes," Weiwei said softly.

I let her help me to my feet. After changing out of my mud-splattered clothes, I sank into the bath Weiwei had prepared for me. "Weiwei," I said after a while.

"Is everything alright?" her voice came from the other side of the screens separating the room.

"Yuxin left this morning, didn't she?" I said absently.

"Where did you say you met Yuxin?"

"I ran into her at the medicine shop."

Weiwei was silent for a moment. "She couldn't have known Sister Chen ran out of medicine."

"Maybe she was just passing by." But as the words left my mouth, I found myself starting to question them.

✦ ✦ ✦

"Xiyan," Chen Han whispered.

I let out a sob. "Sister Chen."

Chen Han reached out a frail hand to me, and I quickly took it in my own. Weiwei, Yuxin, Fei Ziyi and I all stood around her bed. The sun had just set, and the rain had started up again. The downpour continued to come down hard outside, and the sounds of the drops hitting the roof were loud.

"You need to look after your own health," Chen Han said weakly. "I heard from Ziyi that you fainted outside yesterday."

I blinked back my tears as I offered her a smile. "I'll be more careful next time."

"What did the doctor say?" Yuxin asked quietly. "Sister Chen, will you be able to get better soon?"

"I'm dying," Chen Han said simply. "No amount of medicine can save me now."

I inhaled sharply at the same time Weiwei let out a sob.

"But the doctor was just here yesterday!" I shook my head, refusing to believe it.

"The illness is in my mind," Chen Han said. Even though there was still a faint smile on her face, there was no strength left in her voice. "I've been hallucinating more and more recently. This morning I could have sworn I saw my late master. I never thought my insomnia would get to this point."

Fei Ziyi just stared at Chen Han. "This doesn't seem like insomnia."

Chen Han just sighed. "My lack of sleep in the past has made me prone to mental illnesses. And now it's led to hallucinations."

Fei Ziyi knelt down beside her, then reached out and gently tucked her unbound hair behind one of her ears. His hands were shaking as he whispered, "I thought you were getting better."

Chen Han let out a tired laugh as she frailly cupped Fei Ziyi's hand to her cheek. "I thought so too. But I'm not angry. I'm just a little sad. If this is fate, so be it. I, Chen Han, don't have many regrets in this life. My only regret . . ." With much effort, Chen Han raised herself up. Fei Ziyi seemed frozen to the spot as she leaned forward to brush her lips against his. Then her body went limp. Her eyes fluttered shut, and Fei Ziyi caught her before gravity could have its way.

"Chen Han!" Fei Ziyi desperately cried. "Chen Han!"

My own cry mingled with Weiwei and Yuxin's. "Sister Chen!"

✦ ✦ ✦

That night, I stood outside on the walkway, leaning against the railings. The rain pattered on the roof above me. Ever since Chen Han passed out, she had yet to wake. Fei Ziyi hadn't left her side, and Weiwei, Yuxin, and I had only just retired to our own room.

"Xiyan," a voice said softly. The sound mingled with the rain.

I hastily wiped my tears away with the back of my hand before turning to find Yuxin standing behind me. "Yuxin."

"Sister Chen is a martial artist," she said with a sigh as she joined me in front of the railing. "Martial artists are lucky if they can live over twenty-five years."

I leaned against the railing. "I don't want Sister Chen to die."

Yuxin sighed again. "Everyone wants a lot of things in life. But not everyone can be lucky enough to get them."

Taking a deep breath, I turned to face Yuxin. "Yuxin, I'm confused." I looked at her hopelessly. "I'm so confused. How did things become like this?"

Yuxin's unbound hair fluttered in the wind. "You've started doubting me too." She let out a sad laugh and shook her head. "Was it foolish of me to think you'd always stand by my side? Weiwei started getting suspicious of me first. Do you believe her?"

"I don't know what to believe." I wiped my tears away as they began to flow again.

Yuxin turned to gaze out at the rain. "Yes, I had a hand in Xiao Ming's death in the village. I only untied him and said a few words to him. He was the one who chose to hang himself."

I shook my head in a mixture of horror and dismay. "You talked him into suicide."

Yuxin's expression was sad as she met my gaze. "He already had the idea in his head that once he died he'd become a vicious ghost. Am I in the wrong? There would only be trouble if we kept him alive. Maybe you couldn't bring yourself to get rid of him, but I could. I've slowly come to realize that the path you and others walk is different from mine."

"Yuxin-"

"That day when Chen Han made me kneel in the rain," she continued, closing her eyes briefly to center herself, "the real reason she made me kneel was not because I had killed those men, but because she thought my methods were too violent."

I inhaled sharply. "That hair stick?"

"I made it," Yuxin said simply. "Now that I was free, I didn't want to be left defenseless again."

I just shook my head at a loss for words.

Yuxin offered me a sad smile. "Let me tell you a story. This is my story. When I was sixteen, I fell in love. The young man I fell in love with claimed he didn't care about my status. He wanted to buy my freedom and marry me. In that horrible place, he was the first person to treat me as a human." She leaned against the railing, reaching out a hand to touch the rain.

"What happened next?" I asked softly.

"He first came to the brothel because he was lonley," Yuxin said, lost in reminiscence. "He just wanted someone to talk to and confide in. I was always overjoyed whenever he showed up-on those nights, I didn't have to be at the mercy of the other customers. As the months went buy, he kept coming back. I could be myself around him. The other men wanted a persona. They didn't want to know my name. I was whatever name they gave me. I was whoever they wanted me to be-an actress giving them a chance to fulfill their desires. But he didn't want a persona. He wanted me to know the real me. Maybe it was because I was young and naive, or maybe it was because I willingly overlooked the signs that things turned out the way they did."

"What happened?"

Yuxin's dark hair fluttered softly as she turned back to me. "He told me he had fallen in love with me. By then, I was in love with him too. He was young, handsome, gentle, and from a wealthy family. What was there not to like? With him, I felt as if I had found a brief happiness. That was the first time I willingly gave myself to a man. He bought my freedom and brought me back to his residence. He kept saying that he would marry me, but the wedding never happened. One day, I found out he merely liked the thrill of such a forbidden relationship. When I confronted him, he already had a new lover: the top courtesan at the brothel.

"He ended up buying her freedom and bringing her back to his residence as well. And me? He had lost all interest in me by then. He gifted me to an uncle of his. That uncle was lewd, lecherous, and a horrible man. The months when I was at his mercy . . . I wanted to die. What little dignity I had left was stripped away. When I heard my old lover had married that courtesan, I was heartbroken."

Yuxin blinked back tears. "Do you know what that kind of heartbreak feels like? What that kind of betrayal feels like? I was still hoping that one day he would come and save me from his uncle. He never came to visit me even once, and now that he was married to another woman, I knew he never would. Eventually, I managed to go out. I sought out a poison master. When she asked me what kind of poison I wanted, I told her, half sobbing, I wanted the most lethal, the one that would grant the most painful death she had. I was torn. I hated him and wanted him dead, but another part of me couldn't let him go. Another part of me still loved him.

"I mixed the posion into a soup and brought it to my former lover and his new wife to expression my congratulations. Their deaths were horrible. It still haunts me to this day. My former love grabbed me skirt in his bloody hands before he died. For days after, I tried to wash out the blood, but the white fabric was ruined. Afterward, I had no where to go. I could only return to the brothel, the very place I had wished so long to escape. That time I worked hard to become one of the highest ranking courtesans in the capital. I worked my way to the top and became Lady Xu Moyue. I was beginning to accept that I would spent the rest of my days in a drunken dream, but then you arrived.

"Thank you, Xiyan, for giving me another chance at life. But in the end, the paths we've walked have never been the same. When I got blood on the purple dress, I was reminded of that. Even if our paths overlapped briefly, we're destined to part. You're still pure, Xiyan. I don't want anything to happen to you. I don't want you to ever have to experience what I went though. But it's because you've never gone through it that it's impossible for you to truly understand me."

Yuxin stepped forward to wrap her arms around me. I held her tightly. When she finally drew away, Yuxin let out a shaky breath. "I'm leaving, Xiyan. I've come to bid you farewell. Sister Chen was right. You need to take better care of your health."

"Yuxin, I-"

But she had already turned on her heel and was gliding down the walkway, her white nightgown flowing in her wake.

"Wait!" I called desperately as I hurried after her. The last thing I remembered was reaching out to grab Yuxin's arm, and then the world tipped sideways. The words, I just want you to be my good sister again, were never able to make it out of my mouth as everything faded to black.

✦ ✦ ✦

The next morning in the demon realm was the same as every other morning. Once a day, I'd go with the other smoke-like demons, and we'd all descended to where the wicked souls were being punished. After a human died in the human realm, if they had committed foul deeds during their life, their soul would be sent here to be punished for eternity.

I floated through the door of the first cell into a pitch-black void. A torch flickered to life upon my arrival, and I carefully set down a bowl of murky liquid on the slimy floor. "If it isn't my dear friend," a raspy voice called out from the shadows of the cell.

"Little Tang," I greeted the ghost. "I hope you've been well."

"Well?" the ghost cackled. There was the sound of feet squelching through the slime on the floor, and a ghost emerged from the darkness. His gray skin sagged from his bones as he lumbered forward. "Look at me," he rasped. "Look at me!" The moment the words left his mouth, pus burst from the swollen abscesses covering his body and splattered onto the already befouled floor.

I just floated there, disgusted and very glad that demons have no sense of smell.

"Look at me!" the ghost bellowed again, more pus dripping from his abscesses.

I looked at the ghost sadly. "You were vain during your life. You didn't care about anyone other than yourself. You didn't even care when your father died. Instead of attending his funeral, you sat in front of your mirror."

"Look at me!" the ghost choked as the large lumps growing in his throat finally got the better of him.

"Enjoy your meal," I said before turning away.

The next cell I entered was significantly cleaner than the last. "Little Wang," I greeted as I set another tray down on the floor.

There was a roar as the ghost emerged from the darkness. Flames blazed from the ghost's mouth as he choked on the ash filling his throat and lungs. I sighed. "I know you can't speak when you're angry. But you were greedy during your life as a human. When the poor and less fortunate begged you for money, you kicked them away and had your servants beat them in the streets. Now you can't issue any such orders again."

The ghost just roared at me, and tongues of flame shot through my body of smoke. I winced as I turned to leave.

When I finished bringing food to all the ghosts I was assigned to look after, I floated back out of the cell block.

✦ ✦ ✦

I awoke to Weiwei frantically shaking my shoulders.

I sat bolt upright and blinked as the light stung my swollen eyes. I was sitting on the wooden planks of the walkway that encircled the entire second story. The rain had stopped long ago, and the sky was a hazy blue.

I grabbed Weiwei's shoulders. "Yuxin! Where's Yuxin?"

Weiwei blinked at me. "Yuxin?"

I quickly jumped to my feet, my head throbbed painfully as I leaned against the railing. I scanned the yard, but it was completely empty. I sprinted into our room, and with a sinking feeling I found that Yuxin's sword was nowhere to be seen. I drew in one shaky breath after another as I frantically moved to look through the drawers. Other than her sword, all of Yuxin's other belongings were still here. I pulled open another drawer. No-her purple dress was gone as well. My hand fell away as I sank back onto my knees.

I sat alone in the room as Weiwei made breakfast. When she finished, Weiwei brought the food up, and I joined her in Chen Han and Fei Ziyi's room.

"Did you hear what happened?" I asked quietly.

Fei Ziyi nodded. "Xia Yuxin's gone."

I dropped my gaze. "I saw her last night. She told me that she was going to leave. I tried to stop her, and she knocked me out." Something about bringing up Yuxin made my heart clench painfully. "How's Sister Chen?"

Fei Ziyi shook his head. He had developed dark circles under his own eyes. "She hasn't gotten any better." Suddenly, he turned and looked out the window. His eyes were narrowed.

"What's wrong?" Weiwei asked worriedly.

Fei Ziyi picked up his sword from where it was leaning against the wall. "Stay here. I'll be right back."

Once Fei Ziyi had disappeared from the room, Weiwei and I exchanged a glance. Fortunately, we didn't have to wait long for him to return.

"My cousin sent me a letter," Fei Ziyi informed us as if he couldn't quite believe it.

I didn't even bother to hide my surprise. "Brother Gao? Did he come all the way here?"

Fei Ziyi shook his head. "Of course he didn't come here himself. He sent a messenger to deliver it."

"Have you looked at it yet?" Weiwei asked quickly.

Fei Ziyi pulled the letter out of its envelope. "Cousin," he read aloud, "take this letter as a warning. I have spent a number of years in Jingcheng, and during my investigations of the Gao family's downfall, I stumbled upon other shady practices happening in the capital. The lady who's living with you now, Xia Yuxin, is Jingcheng's famous Lady Xu Moyue.

"Lady Xu is famous. But do you know how she rose to fame so quickly? All her competitors died. People believed the brothel had a ghost problem and never suspected it to be the work of a human. What's more, from my investigations, Miss Xia can be linked to the death of Young Master Wen and his wife. I fear that Miss Xia is dangerous. I advise you to heed my words and proceed with caution around her." Fei Ziyi reached the end of the letter and stared blankly at the page.

I stood there, frozen.

"Xiyan?" Weiwei's worried voice seemed to echo from an entire world away.

"I have to check something," I said breathlessly. I spun around and sprinted out the door, down the stairs, and across the yard. I only stopped running when I reached the town, gasping for air and clutching a stitch in my side.

When I entered the medicine shop, I hurried over to the counter. "Excuse me," I panted. "Has a girl that looks like me shopped here often?"

The man standing behind the counter blinked as he looked down at me. "She's your sister, is she not?"

"So she has come here often?" I asked with a sinking feeling in my chest. "What has she been buying?"

The man behind the counter gave me a strange look. "If you're really so curious, I'll show you." I watched as the man stepped out from behind the counter and made his way over to a high shelf in the far corner of the room. "Here." The man handed me the box.

I hesitantly took the box from him and looked down at the label. My eyes widened. "Isn't this the medicine that helps someone stay awake?"

The man nodded. "There isn't anything too special about it. Except if you use too much of it-"

"If you accidentally expose yourself to too much of it, you won't be able to sleep for days!" I turned to the man in a panic. "How often has my sister been buying this?"

"Quiet often," the man said, perplexed. "For the past four months now."

I nearly let out a sob.

Before I left the medicine shop, I asked the man behind the counter what exactly would happen if someone took too much of the medicine. I held my breath as the man explained that if someone was exposed to the medicine in small quantities every day, at first there would be no visible effect. However, the real, permanent, and more dangerous effects would take place over a number of months. The lack of sleep would cause a person's body to shut down, and then they would enter an even more dangerous state when hallucinations would start. Chen Han would be trapped in hallucinations until her heart finally gave out.

Even though the warmth of the sun beat down on me from overhead as I walked home, I wrapped my arms around myself as I shivered violently. I felt sick.

When I got back, I quietly discussed my findings with Weiwei and Fei Ziyi. Fei Ziyi's face went pale when I finished explaining. "So my senior is going to hallucinate to death? I never thought Xia Yuxin hated her so much."

I sniffed. "I didn't think so either. But the next time Sister Chen wakes, she won't be completely sane."

The three of us looked over at where Chen Han lay on the bed. Her eyes were closed, and her expression was peaceful.

"If I ever find Xia Yuxin, I'm going to kill her," Fei Ziyi swore as his expression darkened.

I just remained silent and watched Chen Han's sleeping face. For her and Fei Ziyi's sake, I hoped she would stay the way she was right now for a little longer.

✦ ✦ ✦

Crash! I awoke in the middle of the night to the sound of something shattering. I looked to Weiwei through the dark, wide eyed. Weiwei was awake too, and we quickly scrambled to our feet. The sound had come from Chen Han and Fei Ziyi's room.

Crash! The sound came again. Weiwei and I skidded to a stop at the doors to the room and threw them open. I immediately spotted Fei Ziyi standing in the middle of the room. His head snapped around to look at us, and his expression was frightened. "Keep back!" he warned as he desperately motioned for us to stay where we were.

I held my breath and leaned around the door. Chen Han stood on the bed, her eyes frantically scanning the room. Her sword was in her hand, and she whirled on the spot, slashing at the air as she let out a sound somewhere between a scream and a laugh.

"Chen Han!" Fei Ziyi called desperately as he reached a hand toward her. "Please get down from there!" But his words fell on deaf ears as she continued to slash out at the air. "Chen Han!" He tried again.

Chen Han stilled. A split second later, she was standing in front of Fei Ziyi with the tip of her sword at his neck. "Stay away from me." Chen Han was breathing heavily. "I won't let you or Mother sell me. I'm still your daughter."

"You're mistaking me for your father," Fei Ziyi responded quietly. "You're safe here, Chen Han. Your father isn't here. I'm Fei Ziyi."

"Fei Ziyi?" Chen Han echoed blankly.

Fei Ziyi nodded his head, careful of the blade Chen Han was still pointing at his throat. "I'm Ziyi, your junior. Remember? We grew up together."

"Grew up together . . ." Chen Han slowly lowered her sword, and the moonlight spilling in through the window made the metal glow silver.

Fei Ziyi carefully pried the sword from her pale hand and returned it to its sheath. "Let's get you to sleep." As he gently sat her down on the bed, Weiwei and I quietly made our way back to our own room.

Try as I might, I couldn't sleep at all. I lay in bed, completely shaken.

In the morning, Weiwei and I went to check on Fei Ziyi and Chen Han. We quietly entered the room and found the two of them fast asleep. Chen Han lay on the bed; her eyes were closed, and her complexion was even more ghostly than it had been the last time I saw her. Fei Ziyi was sitting on the floor next to the bed, his head resting on his arms.

I inhaled sharply. In the morning light, I could see the cuts racing down Fei Ziyi's arms. It appeared that Chen Han had attacked him in the middle of the night before Weiwei and I had arrived.

Later, when Chen Han woke, her hallucinations took over, and she spent the entire morning screaming. When her voice finally gave out, she sat trembling in the corner of her room with her hands pressed over her eyes.

Weiwei, Fei Ziyi, and I had tried our best to calm her down, but Chen Han kept crying and pointing wildly at the air.

Days went by, and my worries began to intensify when Chen Han no longer seemed to sleep at all. She must have been awake for four days straight, and the dark circles under her eyes made her resemble a skeleton. Every night, Chen Han's screams would cut through the air. I could feel my own lack of sleep beginning to get to me, and I could tell it was affecting Weiwei and Fei Ziyi as well.

One night, as I was lying in bed, staring up at the ceiling, Chen Han began half screaming, half sobbing again. I could hear Fei Ziyi desperately trying to calm her down. Then suddenly, there was the sound of something metal clattering to the floor, and everything went silent.

I sat bolt upright. My heart was pounding away in my chest. Weiwei was at my side as we hurried to Chen Han and Fei Ziyi's room. I stifled a cry.

Fei Ziyi was kneeling on the floor with his arms wrapped around an unmoving Chen Han.

He slowly looked up at us with unseeing eyes. "She was hallucinating again. But this time, she used her sword to slit her own throat. She died in my arms. I don't even know how she got to her sword. I hid it from her."

I clapped my hands over my mouth as my knees gave out. And as my eyes adjusted to the dark, I could see the bloody slash across Chen Han's neck. I dropped my gaze and my eyes fell on the sword laying at her feet.

Chen Han was dead.

Chapter Twenty

After Chen Han's death, Fei Ziyi refused to let go of her body. It took Weiwei and me an entire day of gentle coaxing to finally have him agree to a burial. Even after we held a funeral of our own and buried Chen Han's body in the forest behind the yard, Fei Ziyi still had trouble coming to terms with what had happened.

Weiwei and I did our best to console him, but over the next few days, he became completely listless. He spent his days sitting on the floor of the room he used to share with Chen Han, staring out the window.

"Fei Ziyi," I said quietly as I knocked on the door to the room. "Fei Ziyi?"

When he didn't make any sounds of acknowledgment, I sighed and stepped inside. I set down a tray of food on the table, then picked up a bowl of soup and crouched down next to him.

"You have to eat something," I said softly.

Fei Ziyi continued to stare out the window.

"Fei Ziyi," I tried again. "Sister Chen wouldn't want to see you like this."

"Chen Han is gone." His voice was nearly inaudible. "Xia Yuxin killed her. I'm going to avenge her. I'm going to kill Xia Yuxin." But even after the words had left his mouth, Fei Ziyi continued to sit there, unmoving.

"If you really want to avenge Sister Chen, you'll need strength. At least drink this soup."

Fei Ziyi slowly turned to look at me with unseeing eyes. I reached out and lifted one of his hands to place the bowl of soup on top of it.

"You look a little bit like her, you know," Fei Ziyi said as he slowly lifted the bowl of soup to his lips. "You look a little bit like Chen Han's murderer."

I tried not to flinch at his words. "I'll let Weiwei bring you food from now on," I said, trying to keep my voice steady as I blinked back the stinging in my eyes. "Just remember that you need to eat."

Once Fei Ziyi finished drinking the soup, he turned back to the window. "I'm full."

I quietly took the bowl from him and rose to my feet. I placed the bowl back on the tray and made my way toward the door. But before I could get one foot over the threshold, there was the sound of a sword being drawn, and the next moment, I could see a glinting blade hovering next to my neck.

"Don't move," Fei Ziyi said quietly.

I remained where I was, trying my best to ignore the shaking of my hands as they grasped the wooden tray.

"How do I know you didn't work with her?" he demanded. "Answer me!"

"You know me, Fei Ziyi," I cried. "I wouldn't hurt Sister Chen!" There was a crash as the tray in my hands slipped from my grasp, and I let out a startled yelp as it hit the floor at my feet.

"Don't lie to me."

I stood there, shaking. "Fei Ziyi, please calm down. I understand that you're in pain. We all are. We're all grieving-"

"Fei Ziyi!" Weiwei appeared in the doorway. Her eyes were wide as they met mine. "What are you doing?" Weiwei quickly rushed forward and pulled me away from Fei Ziyi's sword. Then she turned me around so that Fei Ziyi could see my tear-streaked face. "Remember that what people do doesn't always have any connection to their family! Xiyan never hurt Sister Chen!"

Fei Ziyi slowly lowered his sword as he looked at Weiwei and me. "I'm sorry," Fei Ziyi's voice dropped. "I wasn't thinking straight just now."

Weiwei knelt down to pick up the wooden tray and the bowl. "We'll let you rest." I let Weiwei lead me out of his room and into ours. Instead of asking what happened, Weiwei just gave me a hug.

"You should cook something solid for Fei Ziyi," I said after a while. "He drank the soup I gave him, but it's been many days since he's eaten solid food."

Weiwei nodded her head. "Okay." I watched as she walked over to the door. She paused in the doorway for a moment and turned to look back at me. Outside the window, the rain pattered down over the land. It was another gloomy day.

I just gave Weiwei a reassuring smile. I'm fine, I mouthed.

Weiwei smiled back before she vanished around the corner.

The moment she was gone, my smile faltered. I walked over to the corner of the room and slid down against the wall. Hugging my knees to my chest, I cried, and cried, and cried. My tears were silent as they streamed down the sides of my face. Fei Ziyi wasn't the only one who missed Chen Han.

I let myself fall onto the floor and stared at the wall in a daze. Maybe it was time for me to leave. Even though Yuxin had hurt Chen Han, I couldn't bring myself to fully hate her either. She was my sister. She had lost her way. I didn't believe she was a bad person. She had just lost faith in the ones she loved. She was hurting, and the pain was blinding her judgment. As her sister, I should have seen the signs earlier and helped her back onto the right path.

I wasn't sure when I had fallen asleep, but I awoke to the sound of laughter. I slowly sat up and realized the laughter was coming from outside. I made my way over to the window. It had stopped raining, and my gaze fell on Fei Ziyi. He was sitting at the stone table outside with jars of liquor piled on the ground around him.

"Fei Ziyi's drinking again," Weiwei said sadly as she came over to stand next to me. "I don't blame him, but I do worry for him."

"I worry for him too," I said quietly. "I don't think he'll go as far as committing suicide to join Sister Chen, but he's already not in his right mind." Then I turned to look at Weiwei. "I remind Fei Ziyi of Yuxin. I can understand that he probably doesn't want to see me. When I do go out, I'll cover my face. Maybe I can buy a mask somewhere."

"Xiyan." Weiwei turned to look at me. Her eyes were pained. "You don't have to do that. I'll try and talk to him-"

I smiled faintly as I took Weiwei's hands in my own. "Weiwei, my good sister. I appreciate it. But I think it's for the best if I hide my face."

Weiwei squeezed my hands. "You and Yuxin are not the same person."

I offered her a smile. "I'm going to go to town and buy us our groceries for the week. Keep an eye on Fei Ziyi for me, will you? If anything happens to him, Sister Chen will never forgive us."

"Xiyan," Weiwei tried as I let my hands fall from her grasp.

I just smiled over my shoulder as I made my way to the door.

The walk to the town was a long and lonely one. Instead of going straight to all the street vendors selling freshly harvested crops and dried meats, I found a vendor selling masks first. After finishing my tasks, I held the mask in my hands on the walk back. When I reached the front doors, I made sure to slip the mask over my eyes before I entered the yard beyond.

Fei Ziyi was still sitting at the stone table off to the side of the yard. He didn't seem to notice me as I tiptoed past. When I finally reached the kitchen, I began to stash everything away in its proper place.

"Xiyan," Weiwei's voice said.

I turned around and blinked to find Weiwei standing in front of me.

Weiwei jumped backward in surprise as her eyes fell on my mask. "Xiyan! You scared me! For a second I thought you were a thief!"

"It seems like the mask works, then."

"Fei Ziyi is outside," Weiwei pointed out as she helped me sort through the remainder of the food I bought. "You don't have to wear the mask now."

I just shook my head. "It's fine. This way, I can try and get used to it."

When we finished putting everything away, we left the kitchen. Since Fei Ziyi was still in the yard, I decided it would be best if I practiced with my sword outside of the residence's walls. I left the yard using the rickety old ladder propped up against the stone wall behind the house.

I practiced for hours by myself until I could no longer lift my blade. My limbs felt like jelly, and I let gravity pull me to the ground. I lay there, staring up at the cloudy blue sky through the eye holes in my mask. Maybe I'll just lay here, I thought. I felt so heavy. Laying here forever doesn't seem like such a bad thing.

"Xiyan." Weiwei's voice floated over to me, and I turned my head to find her peeking over the top of the wall.

"Weiwei," I called back tiredly. "Could you help me up?"

✦ ✦ ✦

That evening, I was standing on the balcony cleaning my mask when I suddenly became aware of a presence approaching.

Fei Ziyi came to a stop in front of me. "You look like Xia Yuxin," he said. I could smell the alcohol on his breath. "Xia Yuxin is your sister. You were the last one to speak with her. You were the last one to see her. Why didn't you stop her from leaving?"

"I-" I stammered.

"Why didn't you stop her?" Fei Ziyi asked quietly.

"I-I-" I rapidly blinked back the stinging in my eyes.

"Why didn't you stop her?" Fei Ziyi bellowed. "If you had just stopped her from leaving, she wouldn't have escaped! Now that she's gone, who knows how many people she'll kill just like my senior!"

I just sobbed as I took a step backward. I wanted to tell him that I tried and that Yuxin had surprised me. But my words failed me. Maybe it was because, deep down, I didn't want any harm to come to Yuxin either.

After a long moment of silence, Fei Ziyi spoke again. "This face of yours . . ."

Stunned into silence, I blinked as metal flashed before my eyes. I didn't even feel the stinging across my face. My entire body was numb from shock as my blood slowly began to trickle into my eyes. My hand was shaking as I lifted it to my face. It was only when I pressed it to my face that I could feel my split flesh. I choked on my scream. My face had been slashed diagonally from my forehead, over my nose, to my cheek. Horrified, I opened my mouth but then closed it again when no sound came out.

"Xiyan!" Weiwei sprinted toward me. She shoved Fei Ziyi aside as she stared at my bleeding face, then whirled on him. "Why? Why must you do this?" Before he could answer, she shook her head, breathing heavily. "We can't stay here with you anymore. We're leaving first thing in the morning."

I didn't protest as she tugged me into our room and slammed the door behind us.

"What about Fei Ziyi?" I whispered as Weiwei hurriedly rummaged around for medicine. I was trying my best not to cry, but the salt of my tears were already savagely stinging my wound. "He's in no state to be by himself."

"Fei Ziyi is a grown man," Weiwei said shortly. "He should be able to take care of himself."

"You know what I mean."

Weiwei's expression was pained as she took a seat in front of me and began to clean my wound. "How about we write a letter to his cousin, Brother Gao? I know Brother Gao is back in the capital preparing for the imperial exam, but once we explain the situation, I think he'll let Fei Ziyi stay with him in the capital."

As Weiwei continued to wipe the blood from my face, I closed my eyes for a brief moment. Everything felt so heavy. My heart, my head, my will to keep moving forward. The pain was overwhelming.

✦ ✦ ✦

There wasn't a lot I needed to bring with me. Besides the clothes on my back, a small pouch of coins, and my sword, nothing else was essential. The majority of Yuxin's belongings were still in the room, and I found my gaze lingering on them for a long time.

Once everything that I was going to bring was in a small pile in the corner of the room, I made my way over to the window. Mindful of my bandages, I rested my chin on the palms of my hand and stared at the world outside. My mind was blank.

On the way out, I picked up my mask from the table and carefully slid it over my eyes. Not only did it hide my face, but now it also hid my wound, which Weiwei had tearfully informed me would leave a prominent scar.

Before long, Weiwei and I made our way across the yard. The two of us stopped once we reached the doors to look back at the place we had called home for so many months. That entire morning, Fei Ziyi was nowhere to be seen. "He ruined your face," Weiwei muttered darkly under her breath. "Now he has no face left to see us."

"Do you think we'll ever be back here?" I whispered.

"I don't know," Weiwei said truthfully.

The two of us walked around the outside of the wall to the forest where we had buried Chen Han. We paid our respects, then went on our way down the path. My fingers clenched around the sheath of my sword. If only I could forget everything.

✦ ✦ ✦

"Xiyan," Weiwei said softly. "You have to eat something."

I hugged my knees to my chest. "I'm not hungry."

"It's been an entire day now since you've last eaten anything."

"Has it?" I was sitting on the floor of the inn room we were renting. It had been a few weeks since we parted ways with Fei Ziyi. At first, we had mindlessly journeyed as far as the dirt path would take us, and when it finally disappeared, the two of us picked a random direction and walked until we found a town.

"Xiyan." Weiwei's voice drew me back from my daze. "At least let me help you put your hair up." I shook my head, and Weiwei let out a sigh. "Let me apply medicine to your face. You've been wearing that mask-"

"Weiwei." I caught her wrist as she reached for my mask. "I-I think I just need some time alone."

Weiwei looked conflicted, but finally she lowered her hand. "I'll leave you here, then."

Chapter Twenty-One

I lay in the corner of the small house, shivering. I had caught a cold again. In the morning I was burning hot, and now I was freezing. The last time I had been outside felt like an entire lifetime ago.

Even though it had been almost a year since my wound healed, my face was permanently scarred. When we first arrived at the village, Weiwei and I used the last of our money to buy an abandoned, one-room house and fixed it up. It took the villagers a while to warm up to us. Once, when we were helping out on the communal farm, a group of young women laughed at me for wearing a mask. In response, Weiwei shot back that it was to prevent them from feeling jealous that I was much prettier than all of them combined.

But now I had lost the energy to even go outside at all. I had become scared of what lay beyond these walls. I was scared of pain, scared of death. There was a constant pain in my chest. Could one die from fear and guilt? Could one die from heartbreak?

"Xiyan!" I barely registered Weiwei's voice as the door to the house closed behind her. She was at my side in an instant. Her figure swam in and out of focus as I continued to shiver. Weiwei reached for my mask, but I caught her wrist. I lacked strength, though, and she managed to pull it off.

She placed a hand on my forehead. "You're freezing!" she exclaimed, then quickly grabbed a blanket and wrapped it around my body. When it didn't seem to have any effect, Weiwei let out a sob and wrapped her arms around me instead. "Xiyan, how can I make you take care of yourself? This isn't the first time you've been at death's doorstep. When you fell down that steep slope, I was scared half to death when I carried you back. When you got lost in the forest, I was the one who found you and fought off the wolves. Now you won't leave the house or even eat and drink on your own-that's how you've gotten yourself into this ill state! What can I do to bring you back to life?"

Dazed, I just stared blankly over Weiwei's shoulder.

She held me until my temperature finally returned to normal. Finally, Weiwei shakily let me go as she hastily blinked her tears away. Her eyes hopelessly searched my face. "Xiyan, how can I make you want to live again? You can't stay in here forever. I'm in pain as well, but I'm carrying on with living. Look, my hair has even started turning white."

I blinked as her face wavered in and out of focus.

"I'm lost, Weiwei," I whispered.

Weiwei reached out to gently wipe my tear-streaked face with her sleeve. "Live, Xiyan. My only wish in this life is for you to live. I want you to live long, to live well."

✦ ✦ ✦

For the first time in weeks, I had enough energy to go outside. It was night, and the moon was a large pearly orb in the sky above. After collecting a single autumn leaf from the ground, I returned to take a seat on the front steps. My body was weak. Today was the Mid-Autumn Festival, and while I was too sickly to go join the communal festivities, I had managed to convince Weiwei to attend.

Shivering from the cold, I began to write on the leaf. Shen Fanghuan. I miss you.

As I sat there, his voice was a distant echo in my head. He explained to me the special Mid-Autumn custom of his village: We write wishes to the loved ones who are not with us on dry autumn leaves. We crumple the leaves, and then we let the wind scatter the pieces to the four corners of the world, hoping that at least one will reach the ones we think of.

I gently crumpled the leaf under my hands and tossed it into the air. However, there was no wind, and the fragments of the leaf fluttered back down to the ground around me. I let out a soft sob as my voice shook. "But you're no longer in this world," I whispered. "The wind can't find you."

Later that night, Weiwei returned from the celebration and found me drifting in and out of consciousness on the front steps. She brought me back into the house. I wasn't sure when I fell asleep, but when I awoke, it was dark, and I was the only one inside.

It was only then that I heard the faint sound of crying coming from outside. I walked over to the window and opened it just far enough to look out. Weiwei was sitting a short distance away with her face buried in her hands. The light from the moon illuminated the streaks of white now racing through her dark hair.

After a long moment, I carefully shut the window again. For Weiwei's sake, I needed to try to pull myself together.

✦ ✦ ✦

"Weiwei," I said absently. I was sitting next to the window of our small house, cleaning my sword. The seasons had changed again, and now the world was powdered with snow.

"What is it?" Weiwei asked as she came over to sit beside me.

"I've been keeping track of the days. The Spring Festival starts in ten days."

Weiwei nodded her head. "It looks like it's just going to be the two of us this year. How do you want to celebrate?"

"Weiwei, it's the start of a new year. I'll be turning twenty. It's funny how time works. I don't feel any older, and I'm certainly not any wiser."

"When it gets closer to the Spring Festival, I'll buy ingredients for us to make dumplings," Weiwei told me with a soft smile. "Come to think of it, a few of the villagers seemed to have already put up decorations."

I set my sword down to rest my chin on the palm of my hands. "Alright."

Soon, the Spring Festival was upon us. Weiwei and I spent the first night eating dumplings and laughing together. On the village streets, the sound of firecrackers burst through the night.

"Come on!" Weiwei took me by the hand. "Let's go outside and get a closer look!"

I nodded eagerly as the two of us hurried toward the door. But just before I could throw it open, Weiwei hesitated. "You're still wearing your mask."

I blinked. "Why shouldn't I be?"

Weiwei let out a sigh. "Come on, Xiyan. It's night. I think it's dark enough outside that people won't be able to see your scar. Besides, they'll all be watching the festivities."

And so for the first time in a while, I reached up and removed my mask. Before I could second-guess myself, I set the mask down and let Weiwei pull me out the door.

Weiwei and I stood on the side of the road with the rest of the villagers. We stood on our tiptoes, bouncing up and down as we watched the sparking firecrackers. I was laughing as I clapped my hands over my ears. It had been a while since I let myself have fun. I turned back to watch the sparks flash and dance through the night.

"How are you feeling today?" Weiwei asked softly once the two of us returned to our house. We sat on the porch, watching the last of the festivities from afar.

I let out a tired laugh as a rare smile flickered across my face. "Content."

✦ ✦ ✦

"Xiyan." Weiwei sighed as she sat across from me at our small table. "You seem to be thinking very hard about something."

"Do you think if we kept wandering the world, we'd run into Yuxin eventually?"

She leveled me a look. "After all this time, you're still thinking about Yuxin?"

"I want to know hows she's doing."

"She took Sister Chen's life," Weiwei said softly.

"She's not evil either, Weiwei." I dropped my gaze to the bowl of rice in front of me. "But maybe it's for the best we don't meet again."

"You don't have to ever see her again, you know. We could stay here."

"I know." I picked up my bowl of rice and absently passed it from hand to hand. "How about we go to one of the bigger towns to celebrate the lantern festival? It's about time we do something fun together."

Weiwei offered me a smile. "We'll go to the town and spend the lantern festival there. Just focus on eating. I'll plan our trip."

As she rose to her feet, I let out a soft sigh. "I'm sorry, Weiwei. You could have stayed behind with Fei Ziyi. At least if you encountered any trouble, he'd actually be able to keep you safe."

Weiwei looked over her shoulder at me. "If I stayed behind, who would look after you?"

"I don't understand. Why do you stay with me? If you leave me behind, you could still make a future for yourself."

Weiwei let out a sigh. "Are you going to eat your rice?"

"Oh." I looked down at the bowl in my hands. "Right."

✦ ✦ ✦

"Look, look, look!" I tugged Weiwei's arm as the two of us hurried through the crowded streets. "Look at all the colors and people!" The two of us had just entered the town, and the sun was high in the clear sky above us.

"Look there!" Weiwei tugged at my sleeve as she pointed to a bustling restaurant. "Food! I'm starving!"

When the two of us finished eating, we made our way out onto the crowded streets, then split ways after agreeing to meet back in front of the restaurant later. I wanted to inquire about Yuxin, and I knew doing so with Weiwei around would just make her worry.

The first group of people I went up to was a group of youths around my age. One of them seemed to be telling a story to the others, waving his hands around as if to depict an epic battle.

I came up behind the group and lingered there until he was finished with his tale before making my way over to him. "Excuse me," I said as the applause finally subsided. "Have you heard about anyone named Xia Yuxin?"

"Xia Yuxin . . ." the storyteller said thoughtfully. Then he shook his head. "I haven't heard of anyone with that name. I have heard of a Xia Xiyan, though. Do you want to hear the story of how she stopped the Owl and Aspen Sect from being taken over by the Fire Sea Abyss Sect?"

I shook my head. "I've heard that one before."

"I've heard of a Xia Yuxin," one of the other youths piped up. "Isn't she one of those pirates near the coast? Many martial art sect members have been trying to stop them from terrorizing the people and ships in the area."

"A pirate?" I said faintly. "I don't know if we're thinking about the same Xia Yuxin."

"That's the only Xia Yuxin I know of. Sorry."

"What do you know about the pirates?" I asked quickly.

This time it was the storyteller who answered my question. "All of those pirates are former martial artists. All of them either left their sects or got kicked out for not wanting to follow their sect's code of honor. Now they make a living off of terrorizing the merchants that sail in and out of the ports. Even the emperor himself doesn't dare to do anything to them for fear that they'll attack the official trading ships. So far they've left the ships from the imperial fleet alone, but I think it's a warning to him to not get in their way."

"Thank you," I said quietly as I bowed my head to the group of youths. "I'll be on my way."

After asking around a few more times and getting the same answers, I absently wandered the streets. I didn't believe it. I didn't want to believe it. Pirates were likey to have played a part in Shen Fanghuan's death. And now Yuxin had joined them . . . I wasn't sure how long I spent meandering until I noticed it had gotten dark.

I started on my way back to the restaurant Weiwei and I had agreed to meet at, but I realized I was lost. My heart rate quickened slightly as I looked around the crowded streets. Finally deciding on a direction, I continued through the town.

As I made my way further down the streets, the bustling seemed to fade into one monotonous buzz. The restaurant was nowhere to be found, and I finally came to a stop on an empty bridge overlooking a waterway. I hadn't seen this bridge before. I frowned as I looked back in the direction I had come. I shook my head in an attempt to clear it. Then, leaning against the wooden railing, I looked out at the water. I could see my masked face reflected in its serene surface.

But as I continued to look on, a second face appeared next to mine. I quickly turned away from the water to find myself face-to-face with the storyteller I had spoken to earlier.

"Hello." I took a step back, unsettled by his sudden appearance. "Do you need something?"

"Here"-the storyteller took my hand and pressed a handkerchief into it-"you dropped this back there. I've been looking for you since."

I stared blankly at the handkerchief. "I think you're mistaken; this doesn't belong to me."

But when I tried to hand it back to the young man, he just shook his head. "I've been looking for you all day. Don't tell me to leave when I've finally found you."

I took another step backward. "What do you want?"

The storyteller looked at me for a long moment before bursting into laughter. "I've taken an interest in you. I want to know who the girl beneath the mask is."

"I'm sorry," I said quickly. "My friend's waiting for me-I've got to go." Just as I turned on my heel to scurry off, the storyteller's hand closed around my arm, and I staggered. I struggled against his firm grasp. "Let go of me!"

"I just want to see your face," he said as he pulled me back around to face him. "Let me see your face."

I continued to thrash and struggle as the storyteller reached for my mask. Suddenly, I remembered: even though I was an amateur, I had still learned martial arts from Chen Han. My training finally kicked in, and I kneed the storyteller in the chest. He staggered backward, and in the moment of confusion, I ripped my arm out of his grasp and sprinted. Even though I was free, all I could feel was panic.

I sprinted down the empty streets back toward the bustling crowd in the distance. The storyteller's footsteps grew louder behind me, and I yelped as he grabbed me by the collar.

"Let me go!" I reached for my sword, but my heart nearly stopped when my fingers closed around empty air.

"Are you looking for this?" The storyteller held my sword out in front of me.

I made a desperate grab for it, but he just held it out of my reach. My panic got the better of me, and I threw a punch at him. He blocked the first punch I threw, but it seemed his martial arts weren't nearly as good as mine. In a matter of seconds, I had the storyteller lying on the ground, unconscious.

Shaken, I quickly snatched my sword and hesitantly took a step toward the young man. My heart was pounding away in my chest. I couldn't just leave him lying there like that. But just as I took another step closer, he let out a pained noise, and I froze. I gave myself a split second to make up my mind, then sprinted down the street.

I could hear the sound of joyful chatter from the buildings that lined the road. I skidded through the doors of the first restaurant I could find, panting heavily as my heart thundered away.

"Xia Xiyan?" a voice asked. My head snapped toward the sound of my name.

I stared in disbelief at someone I never thought I'd see again. "Master Zeng?" I asked in shock.

The leader of the Owl and Aspen Sect nodded his head as I hurried over to him. "I've been looking for you recently," he said. "Our Owl and Aspen Sect is still in your debt, and I have a piece of information-"

I clapped a hand to my face-I had been wondering how Master Zeng recognized me so quickly. My mask was gone.

A moment later there was a loud bang, and I whirled around as the doors of the restaurant were forcefully thrown open. The storyteller stood in the doorway. "Where's that girl with the mask? I know she came in here!"

Master Zeng looked at me, taking in the look of pure terror on my face. His eyes asked a silent question, and I nodded, swallowing hard.

"Young man," Master Zeng said as he took a step forward, his tawny-colored robes swishing with the movement. It didn't take long for the entire restaurant to fall silent to watch the exchange. "What's troubling you? Today's the Lantern Festival. Why must you disrupt this time of celebration?"

"A masked girl knocked me out!" the storyteller said, enraged.

Master Zeng frowned faintly as he looked at the young man. "And what did this girl look like?"

The storyteller glared as his eyes swept over the crowd gathered in the restaurant. His eyes fell on me, and he let out a laugh. "You! It's you!" He continued to laugh as he pointed at my face. "I thought there would be a beauty under the mask. I never thought you'd have such an ugly scar! No wonder you wear a mask-no one would ever want to look at you!"

"Let's not ruin the festive mood," Master Zeng said. "Are you going to leave, or do you need me to show you out?"

The storyteller eyed the sword at Master Zeng's side, then turned on his heel. He stormed out the door without looking back.

Once the storyteller had vanished into the night, Master Zeng asked me to follow him to one of the tables. I could feel the eyes of the other patrons on me, and I lowered my head.

"What happened between you and that young man?" Master Zeng asked once we were seated.

I let out a breath I hadn't realized I was holding in. "I talked to that man earlier in the day. At the time I was wearing a mask. He found me again not that long ago and tried to take my mask off. I thought I knocked him unconscious, but he caught up to me again."

"If he's threatening you-"

"No, no," I said quickly. "Just leave him be, sir. I'll be leaving this town soon anyway."

"If you say so." Then Master Zeng's gaze turned serious. "Miss Xia, I've been hoping to come across you because I heard about something you might want to know."

Before I could open my mouth, there was the sound of the door flying open. In a panic, I whirled to face the door, afraid the storyteller was back already. But it wasn't the storyteller; it was Weiwei.

"Weiwei!" I exclaimed.

Weiwei hurried over to me and threw her arms around me in a tight embrace. "Xiyan, where did you go? I was waiting in front of the restaurant, but when you didn't come . . . I found your mask lying on the street and thought the worst had happened."

"Weiwei," I sniffled as I hugged her back. "I'm sorry. I got lost again."

Weiwei finally let me go. Her gaze fell on Master Zeng, and she blinked in surprise. "Master Zeng!"

Master Zeng inclined his head. "Sit, both of you. I have something you might want to hear. It's about your friend, Xia Yuxin." Weiwei's expression was still worried as we sat down, but I gave her a small smile. Together, we listened intently as Master Zeng continued, "Miss Xia has been spotted a few times by members of my sect. She married the pirate lord. I have a handful of Owl and Aspen members stationed by the port. They were keeping an eye on her for many months, but recently, Miss Xia and the pirate lord haven't been seen by the coast anymore. You are not going to like hearing this, but a couple of female martial artists have been found dead, and I suspect Miss Xia had something to do with it."

I just stared blankly at the table in front of me.

"Telling you about Miss Xia wasn't the only reason why I've been looking for you," Master Zeng said. His voice drew me out of my spinning thoughts. "Would the two of you consider joining my Owl and Aspen Sect?"

I blinked. "I-I'm sorry?"

Master Zeng just smiled. "Everyone's heard about how you saved my sect from falling into the clutches of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect. It would only make sense that I offered you an opportunity to join. So I've been looking for you to formally ask the two of you to join my sect."

"Can I refuse?" I asked hesitantly.

"Of course. But I'd at least like to hear the reason."

I sighed. "Martial art sects and their petty disputes are the reason why my teacher's master died. In respect for my late teacher and how she never joined a sect, I have no plan of joining one in this lifetime either."

Master Zeng turned to Weiwei. "What about you, though?"

"Xiyan speaks for both of us," Weiwei said softly. "Sister Chen was also the one who taught me martial arts. I couldn't think of disrespecting her or her master by joining a sect."

Master Zeng nodded his head. "Well, if you ever change your mind, my offer is always valid. If you ever need anything from our Owl and Aspen Sect, just ask." Just then, a waiter walked by our table. Master Zeng called him over, then turned to Weiwei and me. "What would the two of you like to eat?"

"You don't have to-" Weiwei and I started at the same time, but Master Zeng just waved us off.

"It's my treat. I'll just order a few dishes, then."
