Gao Yunzhe inclined his head. "I recognized you from the way you walk. What are you doing here?"

"What are you doing here?" I asked faintly.

"Fei Ziyi ran all the way here," Gao Yunzhe said as he regained his composure. "I had to come too, didn't I? He already managed to escape from my watch once. This time I followed him. Someone needs to keep that cousin of mine out of trouble."

I frowned slightly. "Fei Ziyi is here?"

"He is. I've been trying to persuade him to go home, but he won't give up."

"What is he doing? He hasn't really figured out how to get to Yuxin, has he?"

Gao Yunzhe shook his head tiredly. "My cousin spends all his time chasing the pirates around. Even though he's always following them, he still hasn't found an opportunity to get to Xia Yuxin. I don't know much about martial arts, but I can tell that a number of those pirates are even more skilled than my cousin."

"Can you take me to see Fei Ziyi?"

"What-? Yes, of course. But something tells me that if he doesn't listen to me, chances are your words will fall on deaf ears as well."

I let out a sigh. "I have a few things I want to tell him."

"Alright. Follow me."

As we walked, I glanced over my shoulder. I could see Zhao Minmin trailing me from out of the corner of my eye. It was fine. I didn't really expect them to let me go walking around alone.

Gao Yunzhe led me to a restaurant. Fei Ziyi stood at the back of the room, resting his sheathed sword over his shoulder as he scanned the crowd. He was smiling lazily, but there was something blank in his eyes.

I walked over to Fei Ziyi, but he didn't turn to look at me until I was standing right in front of him. He raised his brows as he finally acknowledged me. "Xia Xiyan. What do you want?"

I crossed my arms. "Let's go outside and talk. I want you to be able to hear what I have to say." I turned on my heel and marched outside.

Fei Ziyi emerged with Gao Yunzhe a few moments later. "Just what is it that you want?"

"Fei Ziyi"-I shook my head as I looked at him-"only after Sister Chen died are you finally acting like a martial artist. Only after her death do you try to help her."

"Xia Yuxin killed Chen Han!" he yelled. "I need to avenge her!"

"Chen Han loved you," I said coldly. "You told her that you loved her, but when were you actually present in her life? She waited for you, but in the end, she couldn't wait long enough. Now that she's dead, do you think avenging her will make it up to her?"

Fei Ziyi's face contorted in anger.

I didn't let my confidence waver as I went on, "Chen Han wouldn't want you to die."

"Who said I'm going to die?"

"Fei Ziyi, the pirates are not your match."

"Isn't that why you're here?" Fei Ziyi demanded. "You must have brought help. That's perfect-I'll join you all when you attack."

"It's true that the Owl and Aspect Sect is here. I won't stop you, but if you get yourself killed, Sister Chen will never be able to rest in peace."

Fei Ziyi took a deep breath. "You're right. When Chen Han was alive, it's true that I didn't give her as much attention as I should have. I regret it. I really, really, regret it. I spent too much time worrying about myself to pay attention to her feelings. Deep down I know I'm also responsible for her death. If only I had been more present, if only I had paid more attention-"

"It's too late now to think about what could have been done."

Gao Yunzhe finally spoke up. "Miss Xia, you don't think you're being a little harsh?"

I opened my mouth to respond, but this time Fei Ziyi beat me to it. "Where can I find you and the other members of the Owl and Aspen Sect? I want to help strategize."

"The first inn from the entrance of the town," I said shortly. "You can find us there." When no one else said anything, I turned and walked away.

After a few minutes, Zhao Minmin fell into step beside me. I knew she had heard the entire exchange, and we walked in silence until we returned to the inn. The moment I opened the door to our room, I was greeted by Weiwei, who sprung forward to wrap her arms around me in a tight embrace.

"Xiyan," Weiwei said tearfully as she finally released me, "where did you go? Minmin went to find you after you didn't return within an hour. Tian Yong and I waited here the entire day without any news. I-"

"I'm sorry, Weiwei." I dropped my gaze. I hadn't been thinking properly. I still wasn't thinking properly. "It's my fault."

"We found Fei Ziyi," Zhao Minmin said as she took a seat next to Tian Yong. "I suspect he'll show up at our inn soon."

I curled up on the floor, exhausted. The last thing I remembered before drifting off was the lowered voices of my companions mingling into a whispering echo.

✦ ✦ ✦

"Little Tang," I called out as I materialized in the void-like cell. I stood with my feet firmly on the slick floor, observing the rot and bile everywhere. I set the bowl of murky liquid on the floor, careful not to let my fingers scrape the surface.

"Dear friend," the ghost cackled as he lumbered toward me. With each step he took, pus oozed from his grotesque body. Suddenly, the ghost paused as his eyes fell on my human form. "How-?" Little Tang choked out. "Dear friend, is that you?"

I nodded my head as I folded my arms over my chest.

"Young lad"-Little Tang crept closer to me-"it's been so many years since I've last seen a human. Dear friend, show me a human maiden. It's been too long since I've seen a maiden."

"I'm sorry, Little Tang," I said firmly. "You saw many maidens during your human life. So much that your own wife killed herself out of spite. You're here to reflect on your actions."

The ghost let out an enraged bellow and lunged at me with bulging eyes. He clawed at me with his spindly arms, but they passed straight through my smoky body.

"You-!" the ghost roared, but before he could continue, he started choking. I took a step backward as the ghost clawed at his throat. I took that as my cue to leave the cell.

I entered Little Wang's cell next.

"Human, human," the ghost said in amusement. The flames that made up his mouth grew into a twisted smile as I set down his tray of food. "Human, human," the ghost said again, "I want to peel your skin from your bones and wear it for myself."

"Hello, Little Wang. I see that you've calmed your temper."

"The skin of a human is priceless," the ghost continued as his flaming smile grew even larger. "Let me take your skin for myself."

"Goodbye," I said.

As I walked back toward the library, I searched the mist for any sign of Bifang, but the majestic crane was nowhere to be seen. Without warning, the ground around me began to glow. Panicked, I tried to flee, but within seconds, a wall of shadows shot up around me, and the next thing I knew, it was sweeping me away.

When my feet landed on solid ground again, I was forced to my knees. I inhaled sharply as I looked around at my new surroundings. Suddenly realizing where I was, I dropped to the floor in a deep bow, pressing my forehead to the cold stones.

"You," the demon lord's voice rumbled through the hall. "Let me see your face."

I slowly raised my head. The demon lord let out an angry roar, and I squeezed my eyes shut as my human form was blasted apart. Back in my original smokey body, I trembled as I looked up at him.

"Why do you disobey the rules of my realm?" the demon lord questioned from his throne on the other side of the hall. "You're a lowly thing unworthy of a physical form."

"My lord," I started. My voice shook. "I only wish to be human."

Out of the corner of my vision, I could see Lady Hui and the other ghosts lurking in the shadows. She caught me looking and sneered. Even though she wore a human skin, there was something very inhuman about the gesture.

"Human?" The demon lord just stared at me in surprise for a long moment. "You're not the only one."

I stared at him. "There are others?"

"In the past, while shaping a new batch of demons from darkness, I experimented with modeling their hearts after the greatest evil I've ever known: the human heart. I only created a handful of them, and it's been centuries now since one has defied my rules so shamelessly." His face contorted in a mixture of rage and disgust. "Half of them were successes, but why does the other half defy me? Fine, then. If you want to be a human so badly, I will banish you to the human realm, as I did the others. If you think the demon realm is cruel, just wait until you are in the human realm."

Before I could say anything, the demon lord rose from his throne. The moment he lifted his hand, the world turned to a blinding white light.

Everything was spinning, and I was positive I was falling down, down, down. I was falling through the air-falling through space and time itself. I was being ripped away from my magic. There was a roaring all around me, and the light-it was eating away at my body of shadow.

At long last, everything went still. A sky of blue rolled high above me, and green leaves swayed in the gentle breeze. This was the human realm.

✦ ✦ ✦

The sound of loud chatter filled the restaurant. Fei Ziyi, Gao Yunzhe, Tian Yong, Zhao Minmin, Weiwei, and I were all sitting around our small table, sharing our last meal before our attack on the pirates. For the most part, we ate in silence. Zhao Minmin had tried to strike up a conversation but stopped when it became too much of a struggle to keep it going.

After a while, Tian Yong said, "I'd like to propose a toast. Here's to our success tomorrow."

We lifted our glasses-well, all of us expect Fei Ziyi. He let out a scoff. He hadn't touched any of the food on the table, let alone his glass of liquor. But even so, Fei Ziyi had brought out his own gourd of liquor to drink while we ate.

When we finished our dinner, we all rose from our seats. All of us except Fei Ziyi, who had fallen completely unconscious.

Gao Yunzhe let out a sigh. "I knew my cousin wouldn't eat or drink any of your food. He's going to be bitterly angry once he finds out I drugged his liquor. But it's for his own good. He's the only family I have left. I can't let him get himself killed."

"Thank you," I said softly. "Fei Ziyi should keep living. I hope one day I'll be able to repay you for your help."

Gao Yunzhe shook his head. "You helped free me from those traffickers. Let's call ourselves even."

I smiled faintly as I dipped my head. Now all that was left was to meet up with the rest of the members from the Owl and Aspen Sect to prepare. As I followed Tian Yong, Zhao Minmin, and Weiwei out the door, I hesitated in the doorway and turned to look back over my shoulder at Fei Ziyi and Gao Yunzhe.

Gao Yunzhe caught my eye and motioned for me to follow my friends. Goodbye, Brother Gao, I mouthed.

He just smiled sadly.

Outside, Weiwei and I walked side by side. The ocean gleamed silver in the moonlight. There was something mesmerizing about it, and I found myself unable to draw my gaze away. We were lagging behind, and Tian Yong and Zhao Minmin had already vanished into the night.

"Weiwei, my good sister," I said absently, "I'm sorry. I'm sorry for everything. I don't know what's real anymore." A silent tear slipped under my mask, and I quickly wiped it away. "I don't know who to trust or what to believe. All I know is that I have to stop Yuxin from hurting others."

"I believe we'll stop her," Weiwei said gently. "We've got the Owl and Aspen Sect on our side."

I turned to face her. "You've always had faith in me. I-sometimes I wonder why you still stay with me. You know that I have nothing of value. I have nothing to give you in return."

Weiwei smiled. "I don't need anything in return. I'm just grateful that you've let me hang around for so long. Between you and Yuxin, I was always the useless one of the three of us."

"That's not true! If it wasn't for you, I wouldn't have even survived the palace!"

Weiwei let out a laugh and gazed up at the sky. "Xiyan, tell me, am I silly? Somehow I get the feeling that this is our last night together. But even when I know the end is near . . . I still can't voice all the words I want to say."

"This feels like the end of a long journey to me, too. I'm determined to stop Yuxin-I want to talk to her and convince her to get back on the right path." I drew in a shaky breath. "But if the pirates get to me first . . . she'll end up in Tian Yong's, Zhao Minmin's, or anyone from the Owl and Aspen Sect's hands. If that happens, Weiwei, please look after her for me."

Weiwei turned to look at me in alarm.

I shook my head. "Yuxin is my sister. I'll sacrifice myself for her if I have to. I've already experienced the beautiful things life has to offer. She still hasn't had the chance to."

We still had some time until we were supposed to meet the Owl and Aspen Sect members, so I changed my course to walk toward the empty docks. I gazed out at the water for a while, then reached up and slowly removed my mask. I turned it over in my hands. Then, taking a deep breath of the cold night air, I let the mask fall into the ocean. There was a heavy sadness within me, and I couldn't even force a smile onto my face anymore.

When I turned to face Weiwei, she inhaled sharply. Demon, her lips moved as she read the scars on my face. "This is what you did that night when I lost you in the forest," Weiwei said as she blinked back her tears. "Xiyan, why? Why did you do this to yourself?"

"All this time, I've been the foolish one. Weiwei, believe it or not, I'm not actually from the human realm. I was originally a demon from the demon realm. All I wanted was to experience life as a human, but I messed everything up. It's about time I put a stop to the mess I created and go back to where I belong."

"Where do you belong?" Weiwei just shook her head. "Demon or not, I don't care. You belong here. You didn't cause any of this. Yuxin's path has nothing to do with you."

I just tipped my head back to let the wind kiss my face. "We should go. It won't do us any good to be late."

By the time we reached the restaurant where the members of the Owl and Aspen Sect were meeting, I was beginning to feel my heart rate increase in anticipation.

"Is Master Zeng here?" I heard Tian Yong ask one of his fellow sect members.

"Yes," the young man replied quietly. "He's upstairs."

The Owl and Aspen Sect had completely rented out the restaurant to use as their base of operations for the night; the building was free of all ordinary customers, and a handful of members dressed in casual outfits patrolled the perimeter outside.

Once everyone had arrived, a few of the members stepped forward to explain the plan. Even though the Owl and Aspen members spoke with confidence, I couldn't help but feel sad. They talked about Yuxin as if she was an unthinkable evil. They spoke about her as if she was a demon without a conscience. And while maybe their words did hold some truth, I knew Yuxin was so much more than that; she was a young woman who only ever wanted to be loved and respected. She had never truly been loved and instead had been abused for the majority of her life. She had to fight for her survival. After being subjected to a life of pain and horror, it wasn't easy for anyone to walk away from that without becoming a changed person.

When the briefing was over, everyone left to prepare for the fight. I just leaned against the wall, lost in thought. If I had never been banished from the demon realm or met Yuxin, would she have been sent to the palace as a maid instead of me?

I had been wrong about the human realm. It wasn't the perfect place I had read about in the stories. Maybe parts of it were beautiful, but that beauty couldn't last forever. There was love and happiness as well, but was all the pain and heartache worth it? My fingers absently tightened around the sheath of my sword. Morning was rapidly approaching. It was time to go.

Chapter Twenty-Six

I drew my sword as I stood on the dock with the Owl and Aspen members. We would fight until the pirates surrendered. Now, as we gathered on the dock, the pirates stood on the deck of their ships, cursing at us as they brandished their swords.

The moment the sun began to show its head over the distant horizon, we all leaped onto the ships, and fighting erupted in a roar. As I crossed blades with the first pirate and then the next, I desperately scanned the deck for Yuxin. She was on this boat somewhere. Could she be hiding below deck?

I felt a gentle tug on my sleeve, and I turned to find Weiwei standing by my side. She already had a deep gash across her forehead, and her eyes were worried as she scanned the commotion around us. "There!" Weiwei suddenly pointed.

I followed her finger to the upper deck behind us. Yuxin was casually leaning against the railing as she watched the fighting play out below. Everything dulled around me as Yuxin's eyes met mine. She was dressed in black, and the fabric of her dress fluttered around her pale body.

Yuxin just smiled as I climbed the stairs and came to a staggering stop on the opposite side of the deck.

"Yuxin," I panted as I stared at her.

"Xiyan," Yuxin greeted me. Her unbound hair danced on the wind as she looked past me to Weiwei, who was standing a short distance away. "And you . . . of course you're still with her. Have you told her yet?" I looked from Yuxin to Weiwei in confusion, but Weiwei's stoic expression gave nothing away. Yuxin took a step toward the two of us. "Are you here to kill me, Xiyan?" she asked with a smile.

"I don't want to kill you," I whispered. "But I'm here to tell you to stop you. You killed so many people."

Something flashed in Yuxin's eyes. "Xiyan, my entire life, I've had nothing. I've never been truly loved. Now, the only thing I want is to become the hero from the story. I just want to become the hero my younger self thought I could be and hoped to be before everything went the way it did. I killed the pirate lord. Now, I'm the one in control here. The pirates are at my beck and call, and I'm starting to think that maybe I can make it happen after all."

"Have you heard what the people have been calling you, Yuxin?" I blinked back my tears. "They're calling you a demon! I knew you wanted to be a hero. And I supported you. But what you're doing now is not what a hero does. I don't want to hurt you, but whenever I think of Fan Wanqi and everyone else who died at your hand, I feel so guilty." I clutched my chest as I tearfully shook my head. "I feel like I'm being ripped apart from the inside."

Yuxin's eyes were sad as she lifted an arm. "Do you recognize this dress?"

I blinked as I looked closer at the flowing black fabric. "That's the purple one!"

"The blood left a permanent stain, so I dyed it black. This way, it will never be dirtied again." Something sad flickered behind Yuxin's eyes as she slowly drew her sword from its sheath. "You've chosen your path, Xiyan. And I've chosen mine."

I just shook my head hopelessly. "Yuxin-" But before I could continue, Yuxin charged at me. I quickly dodged her swing and raised my sword. Weiwei was at my side in an instant, and the two of us fought side by side as Yuxin continued to attack. Weiwei hissed in pain as Yuxin's blade slashed her cheek.

Then Weiwei let out a startled sound as Yuxin forcefully knocked the sword out of her hand. Weiwei jumped backward, but I already knew what Yuxin was going to do before she even moved. I threw my sword to the ground. A split second after I threw myself in front of Weiwei, she wrapped her arms around me and spun me around. The next second, I was crying out in pain as the tip of Yuxin's blade pierced through my chest.

My vision blurred with red as I let out a cry. Yuxin's sword had cut clean through Weiwei's back, the tip lodged just below my shoulder. Weiwei held me tightly, and a dull ringing filled my head as blood dribbled from her mouth. Her brow furrowed in pain as Yuxin withdrew her sword in one swift motion.

"Weiwei!" I sobbed as we both collapsed to the floor. "Weiwei, why?"

She just gave me a pained smile. Her clothes were stained red as her blood continued to seep from her wound. "Xiyan," she managed to say before her words were torn away in a series of violent coughs. Her blood splattered onto the deck.

My vision swam with tears as I cradled Weiwei in my arms. I let out a sob.

"Xiyan," Weiwei choked again, but before I could say anything, Weiwei's body went limp. Her tear-filled eyes were wide and unseeing as they reflected the clear sky.

"Weiwei!" I sobbed as I hugged her tightly. It felt as if there was a knife twisting into my heart. It was difficult to breathe.

Yuxin seemed to recover from her shock. "I didn't want to hurt you, Xiyan. But Weiwei . . . oh, Weiwei. Weiwei's pitiful, isn't she?" Her tone was laced with faint amusement.

"What do you mean?" The entire world had blurred around me.

"I'm the one who took Weiwei's letters," Yuxin said. She rummaged through the pockets in her sleeves before tossing a handful of papers onto the floor in front of me. "At first I was worried she was investigating me, but once I read their content, I thought if I needed to kill her one day, I could give them to you on her behalf."

I held my breath as I reached out with a trembling hand toward one of the papers. I wiped my eyes with a hand covered in Weiwei's blood and began to read:

Xiyan, I don't know how to tell you this, but I love you. I've been in love with you for years now. You've added color to my monochrome life and made every day worth living. In the palace, I was never brave enough to tell you. I'm not brave. I never have been, but I don't regret not telling you because then you fell in love with Gardener Shen. He made you happy in ways I couldn't. I was truly happy for the two of you. Ever since you fell in love with him, I knew your heart only had him. My heart only had you, but I can never tell you. I'm afraid if I speak up, I'll no longer get to stay by your side. All I want is for you to live and be happy.

I stared at the ink for a long moment before I quickly reached for one of the other pieces of paper. I smoothed it out, or at least I tried to, but it proved very difficult with how violently my hands were shaking.

Xiyan, I think I've fallen in love with you. I think I've driven myself crazy. All I can do is write out everything I can't say out loud. You've always been so close yet forever out of my reach. But you never belonged to anyone, Xiyan. You don't belong to anyone but yourself. Your path is yours to decide, and anywhere you want to go, I'm willing to follow you. I was never brave, but I will always be brave for you.

I reached for the next letter.

Xiyan, I love you.

My tears were flowing again as I stared at Weiwei's handwriting. I reached for yet another one of the letters, but just as my fingers closed around the page, Yuxin put her foot down on it. I struggled in vain to free the paper.

Then ever so slowly, I raised my gaze to look up at Yuxin. "You killed her," I breathed.

Yuxin just wiped the blood from her sword on her dress.

I let out a scream, but it was a choked and muffled sound. Out of the corner of my vision, I searched for Tian Yong and Zhao Minmin, but the fighting was still going on the lower deck. I closed my eyes, and my breathing came in uneven, shuddering breaths.

Yuxin placed her still-bloodied sword to my neck. "I don't want to kill you, Xiyan, but I won't let you stop me either."

I just shook my head as my vision blurred. I reached for Weiwei's lifeless hand, but suddenly something flashed out of the corner of my vision. I didn't give myself a moment's hesitation as I sprang to my feet. I threw myself in front of Yuxin, and pain sliced through me. I gritted my teeth and forced myself to look up. Fei Ziyi stared back at me. Shock flickered across his face for a brief moment before he withdrew his sword from my chest.

"Xia Yuxin!" Fei Ziyi bellowed. "I'm going to kill you!"

Tian Yong and Zhao Minmin leaped onto the upper deck to drag Fei Ziyi backward, crying "That's Xiyan, not Yuxin!"

"Yuxin . . ." I turned around to face her. My blood had splattered onto her face, and I took a pained step toward her. She was shaking her head in shock and disbelief.

I took one step forward after another. Yuxin caught me as I collapsed into her arms. Her face was drained of color. "Xiyan!" As Yuxin brushed strands of my hair away from my face, I grabbed her sword in one swift motion, pushed her away in another, and sank the sword into my chest.

"Xiyan!" Yuxin screamed as she frantically tried to withdraw the sword, but I held it firmly in place. The sword was slick with my blood as my palms were sliced open.

"Yuxin," I whispered, my voice labored. She knelt in front of me, sobbing as tears streamed down her face. "When you said that no one's ever truly loved you, that isn't true; I loved you. You're my sister. But now I'm dying under the same sword that killed Weiwei. I'm dying under the same sword that killed countless others. Yuxin, it's time to stop."

My eyes flicked shut, and as my strength gave out, I drew in another labored breath. Yuxin finally managed to withdraw her sword and cradled me in her arms.

"What-?" My eyes snapped open in surprise when Yuxin started laughing.

Yuxin's shoulders shook as she let out another broken laugh. "Xiyan, I never wanted to hurt you. In the end, it turns out I didn't even know what love was." She let out another laugh and wiped the tears from her face with a blood-splattered sleeve. After she gently lay me down on the wooden floor, she rose to her feet. "You've always wanted to see me dance. Let me dance for you, Xiyan." Yuxin slowly removed her black dress. The fabric of her white inner robe fluttered in the wind as she bent down to pick up her sword.

As she began to dance, tears continued to trickle down my face. She twirled the sword gracefully, and soon the fighting on the lower deck stopped. Everyone's eyes were on her, mesmerized as they watched. The only sound was Fei Ziyi's distant yells of, "Xia Yuxin, I'll kill you!"

I realized what Yuxin was about to do next only a second before it happened. All I could do was let out a cry of despair as she lifted her sword to her neck and slit her throat. She was dead before she even hit the ground.

I let out another sob. Both Weiwei and Yuxin lay dead next to me. As I continued to lie there, bleeding out, the sob turned into a scream. There was so much pain. Everything was on fire, and my vision spun before my eyes. There was a throbbing in my head-I could feel my one remaining horn. But when I clapped my hands to my head, there was nothing there. I screamed again as my horn shattered, and suddenly, magic surged through my veins.

Even though my entire body was on fire, I didn't give myself a moment to second-guess as I quickly gathered all of my energy. I could feel it trying to escape me as I heaved myself into a sitting position, but I wouldn't let it. I crawled toward Weiwei, and then, closing my eyes, held my hands over her lifeless body. I didn't care that my life force was rapidly fading. I would bring Weiwei back to life, and then I would do the same for Yuxin.

A bright light began to gather around me as I concentrated. My flesh burned as I channeled all my magic into Weiwei. All the pirates and Owl and Aspen Sect members alike gaped up at us in shock.

"Xiyan!" I could hear Tian Yong and Zhao Minmin shouting my name. But it was almost as if I had sunk deep underwater. Their voices were nothing more than a faint echo through the flames that were tearing at me from the inside out.

Suddenly, there was a flash of light, and then I was flying backward. Not backward, I suddenly realized-up. I was shooting upward, away from the pirate ship. Away from the town. All I could do was look on as my human body collapsed alongside Weiwei and Yuxin's lifeless figures.

I struggled against the pull, but it was useless. When the light faded, I was floating in the middle of a massive hall.

"You!" a voice roared. I trembled in the demon lord's presence. "How dare you!"

Lady Hui stood next to the demon lord's throne, and she merely glared coldly when I looked at her, pleading for an explanation of what was happening. My mind was still a scattered mess. I couldn't keep up.

"How dare you break the rules of the human realm!" the demon lord bellowed. "I banished you to the human realm, but I ended up having to take you back! You cannot meddle with the ways of the human realm; you could have done anything you pleased. Anything except bringing the deceased back to life!"

"Why not?" I cried. "I owe her, I owe Weiwei-"

"Silence!" the demon lord commanded.

I fell silent as the entire hall shook from the force of his voice.

"My lord," Lady Hui said, "please calm down. We got this troublesome demon back before it could cause any harm."

The demon lord glared down at me from his throne. "Get out of my sight."

When he didn't go on, I quickly turned and floated out of the hall. There was only one thought that echoed through my mind: I needed to find Weiwei.

I flew as quickly as I could through the fog and haze. When I finally reached the cave-like room, I nearly choked at the number of human spirits packed inside. Sorrowful wails drifted up to me as I desperately scanned the crowds of people. This was a holding space for the people who were wronged during their lives-Weiwei had to be among them.

"Weiwei!" I shouted. "Weiwei!"

I descended, taking on a human form as I pushed through the crowd. I hopelessly scanned the sea of men and women, but there was no sign of her. I searched and searched and searched, but even after I had checked every last person in the cavern, I still couldn't find her.

I let out a sob. Then a thought struck me: maybe Weiwei herself never thought she had been wronged during her life. If that was the case, she wouldn't even be here in the demon realm. She would have ascended. And I . . . I would never see her again.

I floated there in a daze. But then . . . what about Yuxin?

I hurried into the second chamber. "Yuxin!" I yelled. "Yuxin!"

"Stop yelling," a demon said in annoyance as it drifted over to me. "Is Xia Yuxin the one you're looking for? She was placed in a cell to undergo her punishment days ago."

I instantly turned and made my way to the cells.

When I finally found her, I braced myself as I floated into the void-like cell. Yuxin sat in the middle of it, alone in the darkness. At my arrival, she warily looked up at me.

I transformed back into Xia Xiyan before taking a seat across from her. I let out a sob. "Yuxin."

"Xiyan?" Yuxin shook her head as she stared at me. "You were the demon all along!"

I silently nodded my head.

Yuxin let out a broken laugh. "This is what I deserve. I'll take my punishment without any complaints."

"I'll stay with you," I said through my tears.

"I never wanted things to end like this," Yuxin whispered as a tear slid down her own face.

I just smiled sadly. "For as long as you're in the demon realm, I'll accompany you."

✦ ✦ ✦

"How are they, Bifang?" I asked as the magnificent crane landed in front of me.

Perching on its single leg, Bifang ruffled its feathers. "I found all of the humans you asked about. Tian Yong and Zhao Minmin have gotten married. They've both withdrawn from the martial arts world and live contentedly with their two children. Fei Ziyi is following Gao Yunzhe, who just took the imperial exam. Even though his cousin is now part of the court, the Fei lad spends most of his time drunk and moping around. Master Zeng and the Owl and Aspen Sect have been overtaken by the Wandering Fox Sect. Master Huang of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect has retired after violently assassinating a pirate who secretly worked at the palace."

I let out a sigh. "Thank you for checking on them for me, Bifang. I won't ask you to visit the human realm again."

"Are you sure?" Bifang angled its feathery head to the side. "I don't mind."

"I think it's for the best if the rest is kept a mystery."

"I wish I could ascend to the upper realms and check on Hu Qiuwei for you," Bifang said regretfully, "but I'm still banished."

"I know. Thank you, Bifang. For everything."

"Where are you off to now?" Bifang inquired, hopping after me as I started on my way through the fog.

"The library."

"That's right, you've been working on your own book about your experiences in the human realm."

I nodded. "It's been a few years now, and I'm nearly done with it. I think it will be on the shelf soon. That way, at least one of the books in the library will tell the truth about the human realm."

"Where are you going after the library?" Bifang called as I floated over the threshold.

"I'll go see Yuxin," I said simply.
